Tawatur of the Quran's Chapters and Parts
Defining the tawatur of Quranic divisions and its implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the basis for the tawatur of the Quran's surahs and parts and apply it to determine that entire Quranic structure is qat'i (certain) in transmission.

Core Idea
The Quran's division into surahs and verses is transmitted with certainty (tawatur) by customary practice, grounding all rulings on its exact words.

The Quran is not just a collection of verses; its precise division into surahs, verse beginnings and endings is part of the revelation. This passage establishes that this division is mutawatir (indubitable) because the Muslim community has always taken care to know each surah and part for their great reward. The Hanafi usul principle here is that customary practice (ʿādah) creates certainty in transmission, which is essential for attaching fiqh rulings to the exact wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of tawatur
The passage asserts that the beginnings, endings, and every part of the Quran (every surah and its components) are transmitted with certainty. Recognize that this covers the entire textual structure, not just the words.
This includes surah boundaries, verse markers, and even the division into ajza and manazil that carry great reward.
2
Understand the basis: ʿādah (customary practice)
The proof for this tawatur is that customary practice ('ādah) dictates that the community has consistently verified each surah and part due to the immense reward for recitation, writing, and memorization. This widespread, continuous practice yields certainty.
In Hanafi usul, ʿādah is a recognized source of certainty when it is consistent and all-encompassing.
3
Connect to fiqh rulings
The passage explicitly states that rulings (ahkām) are attached to the words (alfādh) and meanings (maʿānī) of the Quran. Because of this, the exact divisions must be certain; otherwise, rulings could be tied to misidentified verses.
For example, the ruling of sajda tilāwah depends on knowing the exact verse boundaries where prostration is required.
4
Recognize the authoritative support
The passage cites al-Itqān (a source by al-Suyūṭī) and declares the view that the entire Quranic structure is mutawātir as the ṣaḥīḥ (correct) and mukhtār (chosen) position. This indicates the strength of this principle in Hanafi usul.
Even if some scholars discussed minor differences about certain āyah endings, the overall tawātur of the divisions remains unquestioned.
5
Apply the principle in usul analysis
When deriving rulings from the Quran, a Hanafi jurist must treat the surah and verse structure as qatʿī (definite). Any claim that a verse is missing or misplaced must be rejected unless supported by equally certain evidence. This solidifies the integrity of all Quran-based istinbāṭ.
This principle also affects issues like the number of verses in a surah for rulings dependent on completion (e.g., recitation in prayer).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومباديها وأواخرها، لأن العادة قاضية بتصدي معرفة كل سورة وكل جزء من أجزاء ما في قراءته أجر عظيم، وكذا كتابته، وكذا حفظه ونيطت الأحكام بألفاظه ومعناه، ومثل هذا يتواتر عادة مع ما لا بد منه . كذا في الاتقان»، وهو الصحيح المختار .
And its beginnings and endings, because custom determines the verification of every surah and every part of what has a great reward in recitation, and likewise its writing, and likewise its memorization, and rulings are attached to its words and meanings. And such is customarily transmitted necessarily. So mentioned in al-Itqan, and it is the correct and chosen [view].
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage states an usul rule regarding the tawatur of the Quranic text. The author (commentator) explains that the entire Quran, including its surahs, verse beginnings, and endings, is transmitted mutawatir (indubitably continuous) through customary practice. This is because the Muslim community has always taken great care in knowing each surah and its boundaries, as they carry immense reward. The rulings of fiqh are attached to the exact words and meanings, so it is necessary that this knowledge be established with certainty. The author cites al-Itqan as support for this being the correct and chosen position. This principle is foundational because it establishes that the division into surahs and verses is part of the revealed text, not a later addition.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): Continuous transmission that provides certainty; here applied to the Quran's divisions.
عادة (ʿādah): Customary practice that becomes a basis for establishing tawatur in transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the knowledge of the Quran's chapters and divisions established?
A) Through ahad reports
B) Through tawatur by customary practice
C) Through ijtihad
D) Through consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The division of the Quran into surahs and parts is established with certainty (tawatur) through the customary practice of the community, and this is necessary because rulings are attached to the exact words and meanings.

The Basmala: Quranic but Not Part of the Surah – A Hanafi Usul Analysis
Usul dispute on Basmala's part-ness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of tawatur to distinguish between a phrase being from the Quran and being part of a specific surah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
The Basmala is Quranic but not part of any surah because part-ness requires tawatur, which is lacking.

In this lesson, we delve into a classic usul dispute: the status of the Basmala. The Hanafi school holds it is a Quranic verse revealed for separation, not as part of any surah. The Shafi'i school considers it part of each surah. How does the Hanafi school arrive at this conclusion? The answer lies in a key usul principle: the requirement of tawatur to establish part-ness (juz'iyya). Let's examine the arguments step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested point
What exactly is in dispute? The status of the Basmala at the beginning of surahs (except al-Naml). Is it part of the surah or only for separation?
The dispute does not apply to the Basmala in Surat al-Naml, which is part of the surah by consensus.
2
State the Hanafi position and its usul premise
The Hanafi school states that the Basmala is Quranic (min al-Quran) but not part of any surah (laysat juz'an min al-surah). The key premise: establishing part-ness requires tawatur (continuous transmission producing certainty).
This is a methodological principle: juz'iyya is proven only by qat'i evidence.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi rely on: (a) tawatur of its placement between surahs for separation, but no tawatur of it being part of each surah; (b) the practice of half the reciters omitting it; (c) the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas; (d) not reciting it aloud in prayer.
Pay attention to the distinction between tawatur of placement and tawatur of part-ness.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i objection: tawatur of the mushaf's inclusion of the Basmala proves it is part of each surah. Hanafi response: inclusion in the mushaf is mutawatir, but that does not prove part-ness; it could be for separation or blessing. The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas supports the separation interpretation.
The Hanafi response uses the possibility (ihtimal) to block the conclusion of part-ness.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: In prayer, the Hanafi do not recite the Basmala aloud and do not consider it a required verse of al-Fatiha; the Shafi'i do. The text argues the Hanafi position is correct because tawatur of part-ness is not established.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position: Basmala is recited silently in prayer but is not a verse of the surah.

بالجهر مرة ولا تتأدى سنة الختم دونها (وليست) جزءاً من السورة ، وقيل : ليست جزءاً (منه) أي القرآن أصلاً، وعليه أصحاب مالك (وقيل) هي جزء (منها) أي من السورة إلا من سورة براءة، ومحل الخلاف البسملة التي الله الرحمن الرحيم نقله في الاتقان برواية أبي داود والحاكم والبيهقي والبزار. وإذا كان فائدة التكرر ذلك فيجوز أن يكون هو فقط لا الجزئية ولا التكرر كتكرر فَبِأَيِّ آلَاءِ رَبِّكُمَا تُكَذِّبَانِ ظاهر الإجماع المذكور حتى يكون القرآن مائة وأربع عشر سورة ومائة وثلاث عشرة آية، وأيضاً : أنه خلاف بالإجماع، فإنه مما لم يقل به أحد ولم ينقل واقتضاء الاجماع المذكور كونها آية مفردة في كل محل ممنوع (و) لنا (أيضاً تركها نصف القراء) وهم ابن عامر ونافع برواية ورش وحمزة وأبو عمرو قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره في غير الفاتحة وتواتر أنه ) و على آله وأصحابه وسلم تركها) عند قراءة السور، لأن قراءة القراء متواترة ولا معنى عند قصد قراءة سورة أن يترك (أوّلها فيجب أن لا تكون جزءاً، ويشهد عليه ما روي في الخبر الصحيح من عدم الجهر بها في الصلاة، فإن قلت : قد قرأها الباقون من القراء فتواتر قراءته عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام فيجب أن تكون جزءاً. قال (وتواتر قراءتها عنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (بقراءة) القراء (الآخرين لا يستلزم كونها جزءاً (منها) لجواز أن تكون للتبرك (كالاستعادة)، فإن قلت : إذا كانت قرآناً ينبغي أن تجوز بها الصلاة إذا اكتفى بها عند من يرى افتراض آية وبها مع الآيتين الأخريين عند من يرى افتراض الثلاث، قال : ثم عدم جواز الصلاة بها لأنه لم يتواتر أنها آية تامة فوقع الشبهة عند الاكتفاء أو الإتيان بها مع أخريين في أداء الفرض الفرض، فلا احتياطاً، وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإنه إذ يصح قد تواتر أنها من القرآن، ولم يثبت كونها جزءاً من السورة وإلا لتواتر كما سبق، وجب أن تكون آية تامة قطعاً، إذ ليست جزءاً ،آية فتواتر قرآنيتها مع عدم تواتر الجزئية في حكم تواتر كونها، آية تامة، وقد يقرر بأنه قد خولف في كونها آية تامّة، فعند الشافعي هي مع الحمد لله رب العالمين آية تامة فلم تجز به احتياطاً. وتعقب عليه الشيخ الهداد في شرح أصول الإمام البزدوي بأنه حينئذ ينبغي أن لا تجزى بقراءة الحمد لله رب العالمين، إذ قد خولف في كونه آية تامة، ثم قرر أصل الكلام بأنه قد خولف في قرآنية البسملة مع كون القراءة فرضاً بالإجماع، فلم تجز بها احتياطاً، وعلى هذا ينبغي أن لا تجزىء في كل مختلف فيه، فلا تصح من غير قراءة الفاتحة، إذ لا فرق عند التحديق ثم إنه لا معنى للاحتياط عند من يقطع بالقرآنية وكونها
[Issue: The Basmala is one verse of the Quran, so it is recited once in completing the Quran.] So whoever vows to complete the Quran must recite the Basmala once, and his obligation is not discharged without reciting it if he recites the Quran without it. Accordingly, it is recommended to recite it aloud once in Tarawih, and the sunna of completion is not fulfilled without it. [And it is not] part of the surah. And some said: it is not part of it, i.e., of the Quran at all, and this is the view of the followers of Malik. And some said: it is part of it, i.e., of the surah, except for Surat Bara’a. The locus of dispute is the Basmala at the beginnings of surahs, not the one in Surat al-Naml in the story of Solomon’s letter. [Our proof is] the consensus that what is transmitted between the covers of the mus-hafs in the script of the Quran is the speech of Allah, especially as the Companions included it despite their strictness in removing anything else, so it is definitely from the Quran. [But] it has not been transmitted tawatur that it is part of it, so part-ness is not established, since it was previously stated that tawatur of part-ness is a condition for its establishment. If you object: Yes, part-ness is not mutawatir, but its placement in this place, which is established by tawatur, necessitates part-ness, so it would be part. He said: Its tawatur in the place does not necessitate that, because it was revealed for separation between surahs, based on Ibn ‘Abbas: the Prophet did not know the separation of a surah until the Basmala was revealed to him. This is transmitted in al-Itqan via Abu Dawud, al-Hakim, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Bazzar. And if the benefit of repetition is that, then it is possible that it is only that, not part-ness, nor repetition like the repetition of “Which of the favors of your Lord will you deny?” And Quranicity and part-ness are not established with the presence of ambiguity and doubt. And with what we have established, it is refuted. And it is refuted that even if tawatur in the place does not necessitate part-ness due to the possibility of separation, why should it not be that it is a single verse in every place as the apparent consensus suggests, such that the Quran would be 114 surahs and 113 verses? Also, that is contrary to consensus, for no one has said it and it is not transmitted. And the implication of the aforementioned consensus that it is a single verse in every place is prevented. [And] we [also have] the omission of it by half of the reciters, who are Ibn ‘Amir, Nafi‘ in the narration of Warsh, Hamza, and Abu ‘Amr – said Matali‘ al-Asrar al-Ilahiya (may his secret be sanctified) in other than al-Fatiha – and it is transmitted tawatur that he (peace be upon him) omitted it when reciting surahs, because the recitation of the reciters is mutawatir, and there is no meaning when intending to recite a surah to omit its beginning, so it must not be part of it. Supporting this is what is narrated in the authentic hadith of not uttering it aloud in prayer. If you object: The other reciters recited it, so his recitation of it (peace be upon him) is mutawatir by their recitation, so it must be part. He said: The tawatur of his recitation of it (peace be upon him) via the reciters [others] does not necessitate it being part of it, because it is possible that it is for blessing, like the isti‘adha. If you say: If it is Quran, then prayer should be valid with it alone according to those who consider one verse obligatory, and with it plus two other verses according to those who consider three obligatory. He said: Then the invalidity of prayer with it is because it is not mutawatir that it is a complete verse, so doubt arises in fulfilling the obligation. So [we] act cautiously. And there is clear consideration in this, for if it is correct that it is mutawatir that it is from the Quran, and it is not established that it is part of the surah (otherwise it would be tawatur as before), then it must definitely be a complete verse, since it is not part of a verse? Thus, the tawatur of its Quranicity along with the lack of tawatur of part-ness is effectively tawatur of its being a complete verse. And it may be established that there is disagreement on it being a complete verse: according to al-Shafi‘i, it together with “Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds” is a complete verse? So prayer was not permitted with it as caution. And Shaykh al-Hidad in his commentary on Usul al-Imam al-Bazdawi rebutted this by saying that in that case, prayer should not be valid with reciting “Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds” because there is disagreement on it being a complete verse. Then he established the main point: there is disagreement on the Quranicity of the Basmala while recitation is obligatory by consensus, so prayer was not permitted with it as caution. Accordingly, prayer should not be valid with any disputed [verse], so prayer without reciting al-Fatiha would be invalid, because there is no difference upon scrutiny. Moreover, there is no meaning to caution for one who is certain of its Quranicity and its...
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a detailed mas'ala (issue) on the legal status of the Basmala. The Hanafi position, presented by the commentator, is that the Basmala is a Quranic verse (therefore must be recited once in completing the Quran and recommended in Tarawih) but it is not part of any surah (except the one in Surat al-Naml). The argument hinges on the requirement of tawatur for establishing something as part of a surah. Since the Basmala's inclusion as a verse of each surah is not transmitted tawatur (only its placement between surahs is tawatur), it is not considered part of the surah. Evidence includes: (1) the practice of half of the seven reciters omitting it, (2) the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet knew surah boundaries only by its revelation, (3) the absence of uttering it aloud in prayer. The text refutes objections, including the Shafi'i view that it is part of al-Fatiha. The commentator also discusses the practical implication: prayer is not valid with only the Basmala because of doubt about its being a complete verse, even though it is Quranic. The author engages with counterarguments from Shaykh al-Hidad, ultimately emphasizing that caution is not meaningful for those who are certain of its Quranicity and status.

Key Terms
بسملة (basmala): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' used at the start of surahs and in other contexts.
جزئية (juzʾiyya): The legal status of being part of a surah (e.g., the Basmala being part of a surah's verses).
تواتر (tawātur): Continuous transmission that produces certainty; required for proving part-ness of a surah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do half the reciters omit the Basmala at the beginning of surahs, according to the Hanafi argument in the passage?
A) Because it is not from the Quran at all.
B) Because it is not part of the surah; it is only for separation.
C) Because it is only recited in prayer, not in recitation.
D) Because it was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Basmala is definitely from the Quran but its inclusion as a verse of each surah is not mutawatir, so it is not part of the surah in Hanafi usul.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Basmala: Hanafi Distinction Between Qur'aniyya and Juz'iyya
Dispute on whether basmala is a Qur'anic verse in each sura

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the basmala's status and explain why lack of tawatur of partiality prevents its inclusion as a verse of every sura.

Core Idea
Tawatur of being in the mushaf proves Qur'aniyya; lack of tawatur of partiality blocks juz'iyya.

The basmala is written in the mushaf, so it is unquestionably from the Qur'an. But is it a verse of every sura? The Hanafi school says no, because that would require separate tawatur that it is part of each sura. This lesson unpacks the evidence: the Companions' ijma on writing it, the practice of half the qurra', and the report of Ibn Abbas on separation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The dispute is whether the basmala is a verse of every sura. The Hanafis say it is Qur'anic but not a juz' of each sura.
All schools agree it is from the Qur'an (Qur'aniyya).
2
State the Hanafi position
The basmala is from the Qur'an but is not a verse of each sura; it was revealed for separation between surahs.
Exception: Surah an-Naml where it is explicitly part of the verse.
3
Analyze the primary dalil: ijma and tawatur
The Companions unanimously wrote it in the mushaf (proving Qur'aniyya). However, its partiality is not mutawatir. In Hanafi usul, tawatur is required to establish that a verse belongs to a specific sura.
Lack of tawatur of partiality means it cannot be proven as part of each sura.
4
Review supporting evidence
Half of the seven qurra' left it when reciting a sura; the hadith of not reciting basmala aloud in prayer supports this.
These evidences, though not mutawatir individually, collectively strengthen the position.
5
Connect to practical consequence
If the basmala is not a full verse of each sura, then prayer is not valid with only the basmala as a recitation.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

تركها ترك مائة وثلاث عشرة آية) والسور سوى براءة بهذا العدد ولم تعرف هذه الرواية عنه، والذي في «الدرر المنثورة» والإتقان» برواية البيهقي : استرق الشيطان من أهل العراق أعظم آية من القرآن : بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم وقال في «الإتقان» : أخرج البيهقي بسند صحيح وفي «الدرر المنثورة» برواية ابن العربي عنه قال : الله الرحمن الرحيم آية. وهذان الأثران لا يدلان على المطلوب، والذي صح عن ابن عباس السبع المثاني فاتحة الكتاب، قيل: فأين السابعة؟ قال: الرحمن الرحيم . في الإتقان». أخرجه ابن خزيمة والبيهقي بسند صحيح. وفيه أخرج الدارقطني بسند صحيح : بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم أول آياتها وبهذين الأثرين يتوهم الجزئية الفاتحة فقط (قلنا : عارضه القاطع وهو عدم تواتر الجزئية الدال على عدمها في الواقع (فيضمحل) المظنون، وهذا هو الجواب عن أخبار الآحاد التي توهم الجزئية، بل يجب أن تكون هذه الأخبار مقطوع السهو، وإلا لتواترت. ولذا لم توجد في المعتبرات كالصحيحين فافهم .
First principle: the Book. The basmala in Surah an-Naml in the story of the letter of Sulayman (peace be upon him). We have ijma that what is conveyed between the covers of the musahif in the script of the Qur'an is the speech of Allah. The Companions wrote it while being careful to exclude everything else, so it is definitely from the Qur'an. But it is not mutawatir that it is a part of each sura, so partiality is not established. If you say: The tawatur of partiality is not established, but writing it in this place which is established by tawatur necessitates partiality, so it becomes a part. He said: Tawatur of it in that place does not necessitate that, because it was revealed for separation between surahs, as Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not know the end of a sura until 'Bismillah...' was revealed. If the benefit of repetition is that, then it is possible that it is only for that, not partiality. Our arguments refute that. We also have that half of the qurra' left it: Ibn Amir, Nafi' (from Warsh), Hamzah, and Abu Amr. The reading of the qurra' is mutawatir, and there is no meaning in intending to recite a surah while leaving its beginning, so it must not be a part. This is supported by the sahih hadith of not reciting it aloud in prayer. If you say the others recited it, so their reading is mutawatir, thus it must be a part. He said: Tawatur of his recitation through the other qurra' does not necessitate it being a part, because it could be for blessing like isti'adha. If you say: if it is Qur'an, then prayer should be valid with it alone for those who consider one verse obligatory, or with two others for those who consider three verses obligatory. He said: The non-permissibility of prayer with it is because it is not mutawatir that it is a complete verse, so doubt arises. But there is evident flaw in this, because if it is established by tawatur that it is from the Qur'an, and it is not established that it is part of a sura (otherwise tawatur would exist), then it must be a complete verse definitively. The Malikis said: the basmala in the beginnings of suras (except in Surah an-Naml) is not mutawatir as being from the Qur'an. We said: its concomitant (i.e., the Companions' writing it in the mushaf) is tawatur, even if it itself is not, and this indicates the existence of the necessitated (Qur'aniyya). The Shafi'is said: it is narrated from Ibn Abbas that whoever abandons it abandons 113 verses. But these reports do not prove the claim. The authentic report from Ibn Abbas is about Fatihah. We said: the definitive evidence (lack of tawatur of partiality) opposes these, so the probabilistic is eliminated. These ahad reports must be considered mistaken, otherwise they would have been mutawatir. Hence they are not found in reliable books like the Sahihayn.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul dispute) between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i and Maliki schools regarding whether the basmala is a Qur'anic verse in every sura. The author first presents the Hanafi position: the basmala is definitely from the Qur'an because it is written in the mushaf, but it is not mutawatir that it is a part of each sura. The Prophet's practice of reciting it for separation between surahs, as reported by Ibn Abbas, supports this. Half of the seven qurra' (Ibn Amir, Nafi' from Warsh, Hamzah, Abu Amr) left it when reciting a sura, indicating it is not part of the sura itself. The fact that it was not recited aloud in prayer further supports this. The author refutes the objection that its recitation by other qurra' proves it is part of the sura by arguing that it could be recited for blessing (tabarruk), like isti'adha. He also addresses the issue of prayer validity with only the basmala: since it is not mutawatir that it is a complete verse, prayer is not valid with it alone. The Malikis argue that the basmala in the beginnings of suras (except Surah an-Naml) is not mutawatir as being from the Qur'an, but the Hanafi response is that the tawatur of its presence in the mushaf (the concomitant) proves its Qur'aniyya. The Shafi'is cite reports from Ibn Abbas about the number of verses, but the author dismisses these as ahad and not contradicting the lack of tawatur of partiality. The final ruling: the basmala is not part of each sura, and prayer is not valid with it alone.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): Uninterrupted mass transmission that yields certainty
جزء (juzʾ): A portion of the Qur'an, specifically a verse or part of a sura
قرآنية (qurʾāniyya): The quality of being from the Qur'an (divine revelation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this passage, why is the basmala not considered a verse of every sura despite being in the mushaf?
A) Because it is not found in Surah al-Naml
B) Because its tawatur as a part of each sura is not established, and evidence shows it was revealed for separation between surahs
C) Because the Shafi'is object to it
D) Because half the qurra' recited it as part of the sura

Key Takeaway
The basmala is Qur'anic but not a verse of every sura; tawatur of partiality is required but lacking.

Tawatur of the Seven and Ten Qira'at
Ruling on tawatur of the seven and ten qira'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that the seven qira'at are mutawatir by consensus and evaluate the dispute over the three additional readings.

Core Idea
The seven qira'at are mutawatir by ijma; the three additional are also mutawatir according to most verifiers.

This passage addresses a foundational issue in usul: the authority of the qira'at. It establishes that the seven widely-known readings are mutawatir, and explains that the three additional readings (Ya'qub, Abu Ja'far, Khalaf) are also considered mutawatir by the majority of scholars, despite a minority view that restricts tawatur to the seven.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
The passage begins by stating the ruling: the seven qira'at are mutawatir, and this is the position of the majority of Muslims.
This is the standard Hanafi view.
2
Recognize the dismissed view
A view that these qira'at are merely mashhura (famous) is mentioned but disregarded as unworthy of consideration.
This shows that the author considers tawatur as established beyond doubt.
3
Analyze the dispute over the three additional qira'at
Some restrict tawatur to the seven; others (the verifiers) hold that the three (Ya'qub, Abu Ja'far, Khalaf) are also mutawatir. The passage cites al-Baghawi and his son in support of the latter.
Note the authority of al-Baghawi as a reference.
4
Evaluate the evidence for the stronger view
The son of al-Baghawi strongly rebukes those who deny the tawatur of the three, calling it 'extremely weak'. This indicates the strength of the majority opinion.
Consider the rhetorical force of the language used.
5
Conclude the relied-upon position
The passage implies that the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that all ten qira'at are mutawatir, as affirmed by the verifiers.
This has implications for the authority of these readings in legal and ritual contexts.

Source Text

مسألة : القراآت السبع المنسوبة إلى الأئمة السبعة نافع، وابن كثير، وأبي عمرو، وابن عامر وعاصم وحمزة والكسائي (متواترة وعليه الجمهور من المسلمين (وقيل) هذه القراآت (مشهورة ) ولا يعبأ بهذا القائل ولا يعتد به ثم المحققون من المسلمين على أن الثلاث المنسوبة إلى الأئمة الثلاثة يعقوب وأبي جعفر ،وخلف أيضاً متواترة، وحكمها حكم السبعة، صرح به محيي السنة البغوي في معالم التنزيل، بل نقل عن البغوي دعوى الاتفاق . وقيل : التواتر مختص بالسبع لا غير وفي الإتقان»: قال ولد البغوي : القول بأن القراآت الثلاث غير متواترة في غاية السقوط، ولا يصح القول به وقد سمعت أبي شدد النكير على بعض الفقهاء حين منع عن القراءة بها، ونص على أن تلك السبع، وهذه الثلاث كلها متواترة معلومة من الدين ضرورة أنها نزلت على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (ومحل الخلاف ما هو من جوهر اللفظ كملك ومالك في ملِكِ يَوْمِ الدِّينِ ﴾ [الفاتحة: ٤] فمالك في قراءة عاصم والكسائي ويعقوب وخلف وملك لغيرهم وروي في «المدارك» أن الإمام الهمام كان يقرأ ملك يوم الدين [الفاتحة: ٤] (دون ما هو من قبيل الهيئة، كالحركات والإدغام والإشمام والروم والتفخيم والإمالة وأضدادها ونحوها فإن تواترها غير واجب، هكذا قال ابن الحاجب وفي الاتقان»: قال غيره : الحق أن أصل المد والإمالة متواتر، ولكن التقدير غير متواتر لاختلاف الناس في كيفية الأداء، كذا قال الزركشي . وقال أيضاً: أما أنواع تخفيف الهمزة فكلها متواترة. وفي الإتقان أيضاً قال ابن الجوزي: لا نعلم ممن تقدم ابن
Issue: The seven qira'at attributed to the seven imams (Nafi', Ibn Kathir, Abu Amr, Ibn Amir, Asim, Hamzah, al-Kisa'i) are mutawatir, and the majority of Muslims hold this. It is said these qira'at are mashhura (famous), but this opinion is disregarded. Then the verifiers among Muslims hold that the three attributed to the three imams (Ya'qub, Abu Ja'far, Khalaf) are also mutawatir, and their ruling is the same as the seven. Muhyi al-Sunnah al-Baghawi stated this in Ma'alim al-Tanzil, and even reported agreement. It is said that tawatur is specific to the seven only. In al-Itqan, the son of al-Baghawi said: The statement that the three qira'at are not mutawatir is extremely weak and cannot be accepted. I heard my father severely rebuke some jurists who forbade reciting with them. He affirmed that both the seven and these three are mutawatir, known necessarily from the religion, revealed to the Messenger of Allah. The scope of disagreement is regarding what is of the essence of the word, like 'malik' and 'malik' in 'Maliki yawmi al-din' (Fatihah 4). As for matters of form (hay'a), like vowel movements, idgham, ishmam, rawm, tafkhim, imala, and their opposites, their tawatur is not required. Ibn al-Hajib said this. In al-Itqan, it is said that the essence of madd and imala is mutawatir, but the precise measure is not mutawatir due to differences in delivery. Al-Zarkashi said that all types of hamzah takhfif are mutawatir. Ibn al-Jawzi said: We do not know of anyone before Ibn...
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is ruling on the tawatur of qira'at. It begins by stating that the seven qira'at (of the seven famous imams) are mutawatir by consensus of the majority of Muslims. A minority view that they are merely mashhura is dismissed. Then it presents the stronger position that the three additional qira'at (Ya'qub, Abu Ja'far, Khalaf) are also mutawatir, as affirmed by al-Baghawi and others. A minority restricts tawatur to the seven. The son of al-Baghawi strongly defends the mutawatir status of all ten. The passage then clarifies that the disagreement about tawatur concerns only lexical variations (like 'malik' vs 'malik'), not matters of pronunciation form (like vowel movements, idgham, imala), whose tawatur is not required. It quotes Ibn al-Hajib and al-Zarkashi on the tawatur of the essence of madd and imala but not the exact degree. All types of hamzah takhfif are considered mutawatir. The passage ends with a quote from Ibn al-Jawzi.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): Uninterrupted mass transmission yielding certainty; used to establish the authenticity of qira'at.
قراءات سبعة (qirāʾāt sabʿa): The seven widely transmitted readings attributed to Nafi', Ibn Kathir, Abu Amr, Ibn Amir, Asim, Hamzah, and al-Kisa'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the three qira'at attributed to Ya'qub, Abu Ja'far, and Khalaf?
A) They are mashhura.
B) They are mutawatir according to the verifiers.
C) They are rejected.
D) They are only accepted by Hanafis.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon position is that all ten qira'at are mutawatir, established by consensus of the majority.

Scope of Tawatur: Lexical vs. Formal Variations in Qira'at
Ruling on the scope of tawatur: lexical vs. formal variations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between variations that are mutawatir (lexical) and those that are not (formal) according to the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Lexical differences in qira'at like malik/malik are mutawatir; formal differences like vowel movements and imala are not.

This passage clarifies the scope of tawatur in qira'at. Not every variation in recitation is covered by tawatur. The disagreement about tawatur applies only to variations that change the essence of the word (jawhari), not to variations in pronunciation style (hay'ah). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the principle of tawatur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the distinction made
The passage distinguishes between variations that are 'of the essence of the word' (min jawhari al-lafz) and those that are 'matters of form' (min qabil al-hay'a).
This is a key classification for determining what is mutawatir.
2
Understand the examples
Example of essence: 'malik' vs. 'malik' in Fatihah 4 are different words that change the meaning. Example of form: differences in vowel movements, idgham, ishmam, rawm, tafkhim, imala, etc.
Formal variations do not change the word itself.
3
Recognize the ruling
The passage states that tawatur is not required for formal variations. This means they are not considered part of the mutawatir Quran but are permissible modes of recitation.
Ibn al-Hajib said this explicitly.
4
Analyze the nuance on madd and imala
Al-Zarkashi notes that the essence of madd and imala is mutawatir, but the precise measure or degree is not.
This shows that even within formal categories, some aspects may have tawatur.
5
Consider the implication for takhfif al-hamzah
The passage concludes that all types of hamzah takhfif are mutawatir, according to al-Zarkashi.
This is a specific exception to the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): Uninterrupted mass transmission yielding certainty; used to establish the authenticity of qira'at.
جوهر اللفظ (jawhar al-lafẓ): The essence or substance of the word; variations that change the letters themselves.
هيئة (hayʾa): Form or manner of pronunciation, including vowel movements, idgham, imala, etc.

A) They are not mutawatir at all.

C) They are all mutawatir.
D) They are considered part of the Quranic text.

Key Takeaway
Tawatur in qira'at applies to lexical differences; formal variations are permissible but not part of the mutawatir Quran.

The Basmala Dispute: Tawatur and Quranicity
Usul dispute over tawatur requirement for Quranicity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that Quranicity requires tawatur to evaluate the basmala's status at the beginning of surahs.

Core Idea
What is not mutawatir in its Quranicity is definitely not Quran.

The basmala appears at the head of every Quranic surah except Surah al-Tawbah. The question arises: is it a verse of the Quran in those positions? The Hanafi school, alongside the Malikis, argues that it is not, because its Quranicity has not been transmitted with tawatur. This lesson unpacks the logical structure of that argument and the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i proof from ahad reports.

Guided Path
1
State the contested issue
Identify exactly what is being disputed: whether the basmala at the beginning of surahs (except al-Naml) is part of the Quran.
The basmala in Surah al-Naml (27:30) is agreed upon as a verse.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof (malzum and lazim)
The Hanafi argument uses logical inference: the universal recording of the basmala in musahif (the malzum, i.e., the antecedent) is mutawatir. However, that recording only indicates the lazim (consequent) of being part of the mus'haf, not necessarily part of the Quran. The lack of tawatur for its Quranicity means it is not Quran.
The text says 'tawatur of its necessary consequence' – the malzum is the widespread recording.
3
Identify the opposing proof (Shafi'i dalil)
The Shafi'is cite reports from Ibn Abbas indicating that the basmala is a verse of al-Fatiha and that omitting it means omitting 113 verses. These reports are ahad.
The text mentions several chains but judges them as ahad and not definitively established.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response is that these ahad reports are overridden by the conclusive evidence (qati) that the basmala's Quranicity is not mutawatir. Ahad reports cannot establish definitive Quranic status. The text says such reports 'must be definitely forgetfulness' otherwise they would have been widely transmitted.
This is a methodological application of the principle that ahad cannot overturn qati'.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute has a practical effect on prayer: Hanafis do not recite the basmala aloud before al-Fatiha in prayer, while Shafi'is do.
This shows how usul differences translate into fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آية تامة، لأن برق الحقيقة قاطع للشبهات فافهم أصحاب الإمام مالك (قالوا: لم يتواتر) البسملة حال كونها ( في أوائل السور) لا التي في سورة النمل أنها من القرآن) وما لم يتواتر قرآنيته ليس منه قطعاً قلنا تواتر (ملزومه وإن لم يتواتر نفسه وهو إثباتهم كلهم في المصاحف (مع المبالغة في التجريد عن الزوائد فيستدل به أي بهذا الملزوم (على) وجود (اللازم) وهو القرآنية فافهم. الشافعية قالوا) : روي عن ابن عباس من تركها ترك مائة وثلاث عشرة آية) والسور سوى براءة بهذا العدد ولم تعرف هذه الرواية عنه، والذي في «الدرر المنثورة» والإتقان» برواية البيهقي : استرق الشيطان من أهل العراق أعظم آية من القرآن : بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم وقال في «الإتقان» : أخرج البيهقي بسند صحيح وفي «الدرر المنثورة» برواية ابن العربي عنه قال : الله الرحمن الرحيم آية. وهذان الأثران لا يدلان على المطلوب، والذي صح عن ابن عباس السبع المثاني فاتحة الكتاب، قيل: فأين السابعة؟ قال: الرحمن الرحيم . في الإتقان». أخرجه ابن خزيمة والبيهقي بسند صحيح. وفيه أخرج الدارقطني بسند صحيح : بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم أول آياتها وبهذين الأثرين يتوهم الجزئية الفاتحة فقط (قلنا : عارضه القاطع وهو عدم تواتر الجزئية الدال على عدمها في الواقع (فيضمحل) المظنون، وهذا هو الجواب عن أخبار الآحاد التي توهم الجزئية، بل يجب أن تكون هذه الأخبار مقطوع السهو، وإلا لتواترت. ولذا لم توجد في المعتبرات كالصحيحين في فافهم .
A complete verse, because the lightning of truth cuts off doubts, so understand. The followers of Imam Malik said: The basmala is not mutawatir, in the beginning of the surahs, not the one in Surah al-Naml, that it is from the Quran. And what is not mutawatir in its Quranicity is definitely not from it. We said: Its necessary consequence is mutawatir, although itself is not mutawatir, and that is their complete recording in the musahif, with extreme caution in removing additions. So this necessary consequence indicates the existence of the necessary, which is Quranicity, so understand. The Shafi'is said: It is narrated from Ibn Abbas: Whoever abandons it abandons 113 verses, and the surahs except Bara'ah are this number, and this narration from him is not known. What is in al-Durar al-Manthur and al-Itqan via Bayhaqi: The devil stole from the people of Iraq the greatest verse of the Quran: Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim. And in al-Itqan: al-Bayhaqi narrated with a sound chain, and in al-Durar al-Manthur via Ibn al-Arabi from him saying: Allah al-Rahman al-Rahim is a verse. These two reports do not indicate the desired. What is sound from Ibn Abbas is the seven mathani: Surat al-Fatiha. It was said: Where is the seventh? He said: al-Rahman al-Rahim. In al-Itqan: Ibn Khuzayma and al-Bayhaqi narrated it with a sound chain. And in it al-Darqutni narrated with a sound chain: Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim is the first of its verses. With these two reports, the partiality of only al-Fatiha is conjectured. We said: The conclusive evidence opposes it, which is the lack of tawatur of partiality, indicating its non-existence in reality, so the conjectured is eliminated. This is the answer to the ahad reports that suggest partiality. Rather, these reports must be definitely forgetfulness, otherwise they would have been mutawatir. Therefore, they are not found in reliable collections like al-Sahihayn.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding whether the basmala (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) is a verse of the Quran at the beginning of each surah, except Surah al-Naml. The Hanafi position, supported by the Maliki scholars mentioned, argues that the basmala is not mutawatir in its Quranicity at the beginning of surahs (excluding Surah al-Naml). The key proof is that while the basmala is recorded in the musahif, this recording is not proof of its being Quran if it was not transmitted mutawatir. The author responds to the Shafi'i proof by showing that the narrations from Ibn Abbas and others are not definitive; they are ahad and contradict the lack of tawatur. Since the basmala's Quranicity is not mutawatir, it is not considered part of the surahs. The author also notes that if these ahad reports were true, they would have been transmitted broadly, which did not happen.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmala): بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم, the phrase that occurs at the beginning of Quranic surahs.
التواتر (al-tawatur): Mass transmission, where so many narrators report a fact that it is impossible for them to have agreed on a lie.
الملزوم (al-malzum): The necessary antecedent: the recording of basmala in musahif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi's primary reason for not considering the basmala at the beginning of surahs as part of the Quran?
A) The basmala is never mentioned in the Quran.
B) Its Quranicity is not transmitted with tawatur.
C) Maliki scholars rejected it.
D) The basmala appears only in one surah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, definitive Quranicity requires tawatur; ahad reports cannot establish it.

Al-Quran as Source

Tawatur of Qira'at and Authority of Shadhdh Readings
Establishing tawatur of qira'at and defining shadhdh readings as hujja zanniyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion of tawatur to the seven and ten qira'at and evaluate the probative value (hujja zanniyya) of shadhdh readings.

Core Idea
The seven (and ten) qira'at are mutawatir; shadhdh readings are hujja zanniyya binding in practice.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmawt addresses a foundational usul issue: the transmission certainty of Quranic readings. It establishes that the seven widely-known qira'at are mutawatir, confirms the same for the additional three, and clarifies that any reading transmitted by less than tawatur (shadhdh) still carries binding authority as a presumptive proof. The Hanafi school's reasoning rests on the nature of tawatur – it requires impossibility of collusion, not a fixed number – and on the necessary relationship between the essence (jawhar) and the form (hay'a) of recitation.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish mutawatir from shadhdh
Define tawatur as mass transmission giving certain knowledge; shadhdh as readings transmitted by less than tawatur but still famous. Note that shadhdh readings are not necessarily rejected; they have presumptive authority.
Tawatur is about the impossibility of collusion, not a specific number.
2
Identify the Hanafi claim on tawatur of the ten
The seven qira'at are mutawatir according to the majority; the additional three (Ya'qub, Abu Ja'far, Khalaf) are also mutawatir, as stated by al-Baghawi and other verifying scholars.
Some restrict tawatur to the seven; the text dismisses this as weak.
3
Analyze the dispute on tawatur of form (hay'a)
Ibn al-Hajib argued that the formal aspects (e.g., lengthening, imala) are not mutawatir. The Hanafi rebuttal: the form is a necessary concomitant of the essence; if the essence is mutawatir, the form must also be mutawatir because the transmission includes the manner of recitation.
The text also criticizes hadith scholars who objected to reciters' stopping practices, arguing that those practices are mutawatir.
4
Examine the argument for tawatur via qiyas
The author provides a proof: if the qira'at were not mutawatir, then some part of the Quran would be non-mutawatir, which contradicts the consensus that the entire Quran is mutawatir.
Deniers argue that the number of reciters (seven) is too small; the Hanafi response is that the actual transmitters are countless, not just the famous reciters.
5
Determine the authority of shadhdh readings
The text defines shadhdh as any reading transmitted by less than tawatur. According to Hanafi usul, such readings are hujja zanniyya: they are binding in practice but do not produce certain knowledge. This is contrary to some Shafi'i reports.
Example: a shadhdh reading requiring consecutive fasting for oath expiation is accepted by Hanafis.

وقد يطلق على ما نقل بأخبار واحد عن واحد (حجة ظنية) عندنا واجبة العمل دون العلم (خلافاً للشافعي) رحمه الله تعالى على ما حكى إمام الحرمين وجزم به ابن الحاجب فما أوجب التتابع) في صيام كفارة اليمين
Issue: The seven qira'at attributed to the seven imams – Nafi', Ibn Kathir, Abu Amr, Ibn Amir, Asim, Hamza, and Kisa'i – are mutawatir, and the majority of Muslims are upon this. And it is said these qira'at are mashhura (famous), and no attention is paid to this speaker nor is it considered. Then the verifying scholars of Muslims hold that the three qira'at attributed to the three imams – Ya'qub, Abu Ja'far, and Khalaf – are also mutawatir, and their ruling is the ruling of the seven. Muhyi al-Sunna al-Baghawi explicitly stated this in Ma'alim al-Tanzil, and he even transmitted agreement from al-Baghawi. And it is said that tawatur is specific to the seven only. In al-Itqan, the son of al-Baghawi said: The statement that the three qira'at are not mutawatir is extremely weak, and it is not correct to say it. I heard my father severely rebuke some jurists when they prevented recitation with them, and he stated that those seven and these three are all mutawatir, known necessarily from the religion that they were revealed upon the Messenger of Allah. The place of disagreement is what pertains to the essence of the word, like malik and malik in maliki yawmi al-din. So malik in the recitation of Asim, Kisa'i, Ya'qub, and Khalaf, and malik for others. It is narrated in al-Madarik that the imam would read maliki yawmi al-din. Not what is of the category of form (al-hay'a), like movements, idgham, ishmam, rawm, tafkhim, imala, and their opposites and similar. Indeed, tawatur of these is not obligatory, thus said Ibn al-Hajib. In al-Itqan, another said: The truth is that the origin of madd and imala is mutawatir, but the measure is not mutawatir due to differences among people in the manner of performance. Thus said al-Zarkashi. And he also said: As for the types of hamza lightening, all are mutawatir. In al-Itqan, Ibn al-Jawzi said: We do not know anyone before Ibn al-Hajib who said that, and the imams of usul like al-Qadi Abu Bakr and others have stated the tawatur of all of that, and he said it is correct. He argued with what the author pointed to in his saying. In the margins of Mirzajan, consistent with al-Itqan: The form is a necessary concomitant of the essence because the essence of the word does not exist without it. So if the essence is mutawatir due to the availability of motivations for transmission as you know, then the form is definitely mutawatir. I say: By the category of form is meant what does not differ with differences in musahif lines and does not differ in meaning with differences in qira'at. It is not a necessary concomitant, nor are motivations available for transmitting details of such, so its tawatur is not obligatory. This is nothing, because tawatur is not through writing in musahif nor for motivations of meaning, but the availability of motivations necessitated something that cannot be counted, and it is transmitted by memory. In it, the essence and form are equal except what differs in that a group preserves the manner of its performance, so tawatur of neither is obligatory, like measurements of madd. The truth accepted by acceptance is this tawatur, and this specification is an error of Ibn al-Hajib. From here it is clear to you that the criticism of some hadith scholars against the reciters for their abstention from stopping in some places like 'Qul yaaaa ayyuha al-kafirun' – since this contradicts what is narrated from the Prophet's recitation according to hadith scholars, and they call stopping on it the Prophet's recitation – is not in place. Indeed, the abstention practiced by the reciters is also from the Prophet, so there is no basis for criticism. Rather, this abstention is mutawatir, and what they narrated are ahad reports, so understand. Then this claim is necessary and does not need proof. Whoever is in doubt should look at the centuries. Indeed, the transmitters of the seven, rather ten, qira'at from the time of the Messenger of Allah until now, in every time, their count exceeds the number of al-Batha'. However, to alert the heedless, the author presented the proof and said: For us, if the mentioned qira'at were not mutawatir, then some of the Quran would be non-mutawatir, which is contrary to consensus. The implication is because specialization of some qira'at as Quran without others is arbitrary. All were transmitted equally, and the imams agreed on the permissibility of praying with them, so all are Quran. The deniers said: The reciters are seven or less, and this number does not establish tawatur, so what they agreed upon is not mutawatir, so what about what they disagreed on? We said: This is only true if they themselves were the transmitters, which is denied. Rather, the transmitters exceed the number of al-Batha'. Their attribution to them is only due to their specialization in verifying them and spending their lives in acquiring them, not because they are the transmitters. So reflect, for it is clear truth. In al-Tahrir, it was answered by denying that tawatur is not established by this number, because number is not a condition for tawatur. The author criticized it, saying that a single person is alone in a recitation, and one is not suitable for establishing tawatur. Perhaps his intention was only to criticize the proof, that it does not establish their claim, because if the transmitters are many, tawatur can be established due to the absence of a condition regarding number. There is reflection in it, so reflect. And it is an issue: The shadhdh reading is other than the ten, transmitted from the Messenger by those who do not reach the number of tawatur, even if they are famous in the second century. That is meant here. It may also be applied to what is transmitted by one from one. It is a hujja zanniyya (presumptive proof) according to us, binding in practice, not in knowledge, contrary to al-Shafi'i, as related by Imam al-Haramayn and stated by Ibn al-Hajib. So what requires consecutive days in fasting for expiation of an oath...
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage covers two main legal issues from usul al-fiqh: the tawatur of the seven (and ten) qira'at, and the authority of shadhdh readings.

First, the author affirms that the seven qira'at attributed to the famous imams are mutawatir (mass-transmitted), and this is the position of the majority. The minority view that they are only mashhura (famous) is dismissed. Then the author extends this to the three additional qira'at (Ya'qub, Abu Ja'far, Khalaf), stating that verifying scholars consider them also mutawatir, quoting al-Baghawi. The dispute about whether tawatur includes the formal aspects (hay'a) of recitation (like elongation, imala) is presented. Ibn al-Hajib held that tawatur of the form is not obligatory, but the author argues that since the essence (jawhar) is mutawatir, the necessary concomitant (form) must also be mutawatir. The author rebuts the denial of tawatur of the form by stating that tawatur is based on oral transmission, not writing, and that both essence and form are transmitted by many. The author then criticizes some hadith scholars who objected to reciters stopping at certain places, arguing that their practice is also from the Prophet and mutawatir.

Next, the author presents a proof for the tawatur of qira'at: if they were not mutawatir, some of the Quran would be non-mutawatir, which is impossible. The deniers argue that the number of reciters is small (seven or less) and thus cannot establish tawatur. The response is that the transmitters are not just these seven; they are the scholars who verified and specialized, but the actual transmitters (the masses) are countless. The author notes that the number itself is not a condition for tawatur.

Finally, a new issue: the shadhdh reading (any reading other than the ten) is defined as transmitted by people who do not reach the number of tawatur, even if famous. According to the Hanafi school, such readings are hujja zanniyya (presumptive proof) binding in practice but not definitive knowledge. This is contrary to al-Shafi'i, who according to some reports does not consider them as proof. The example is given: a shadhdh reading may require consecutive days in fasting for expiation of an oath.

Key Terms
القراءة الشاذة (al-qira'a al-shadhdha): A reading transmitted by a number less than tawatur, even if famous among early scholars.
التواتر (al-tawatur): Mass transmission that yields certain knowledge.
الهيئة (al-hay'a): The formal aspects of recitation such as movements, idgham, ishmam, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following best describes the authority of a shadhdh reading?
A) It is not a proof at all.
B) It is a hujja zanniyya binding in practice.
C) It is mutawatir.
D) It is only for recitation, not for rulings.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds the tawatur of the ten qira'at and treats shadhdh readings as presumptive proofs binding in practice.

Tawatur of Form in Quranic Readings
Logical argument for tawatur of form

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi argument that the form of Quranic readings is mutawatir and evaluate the objection of Ibn al-Hajib.

Core Idea
If the substance is mutawatir, its form is mutawatir by necessity.

This passage addresses a key usul question: are the precise manners of recitation (hay'a) of the Quran transmitted with the same certainty as the words themselves? The Hanafi school insists they are, because the form is inseparable from the substance, and the motives for preservation were equally abundant. We will dissect the logical argument and the refutation of Ibn al-Hajib's skepticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
The passage asserts that the form (hay'a) is mutawatir. Note that 'hay'a' refers to aspects like prolongation that do not alter the script or meaning.
The basis is that the substance (jawhar) is mutawatir.
2
Understand the Necessary Concomitance
Recognize the logical relationship: the form is a necessary concomitant (lazim) of the substance. If A (substance) is transmitted with certainty, and B (form) necessarily accompanies A, then B is also transmitted with certainty.
This is the central argument from the author.
3
Consider the Objection
Ibn al-Hajib objects that the form is not a necessary concomitant, and there is no abundant motive (tawaffur al-dawa'i) to transmit details like the length of prolongation.
This challenges the 'motive' part of the tawatur condition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The response argues that tawatur was not achieved through writing but through oral memory. Both substance and form were transmitted by countless individuals. The number of transmitters is not a condition for tawatur.
The author also cites consensus on the permissibility of praying with all qira'at as evidence.
5
Examine the Practical Consequence
If the form were not mutawatir, some aspects of Quranic recitation would be doubtful, affecting the authority of the qira'at. The passage also defends the qurra' against hadith scholars' criticism.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

والسلام عند أهل الحديث، وسموا الوقف عليه قراءة النبي ليس في محله فإن الامتناع الذي عليه القراء أيضاً من النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، فلا وجه للنكير، بل هذا الامتناع متواتر، وما نقلوا أخبار آحاد فافهم. ثم هذا المدعي ضروري لا يحتاج فيه إلى الدليل ومن كان في ريب فعليه بملاحظة القرون فإن النقلة للقراءات السبعة بل العشرة من لدن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم إلى هذا الآن في كل وقت بكونها قرآناً دون غيرها (تحكم) فإن الكل نقلت على السواء، وأجمع الأئمة بجواز الصلاة بها، فكلها قرآن. المنكرون (قالوا : القراء سبعة أو أقل) وهذا العدد لا ينعقد به التواتر فلا يكون ما اتفقوا عليه متواتراً، فما ظنك بما اختلفوا فيه (قلنا) هذا إنما يتم لو كانوا هم النقلة، وهو ممنوع، بل النقلة أزيد من عدد البطحاء و (نسبتها إليهم إنما هي لاختصاصهم بالتصدي) لها وإفناء العمر في اكتسابها (لا لأنهم) هم مقصوده القدح في الدليل فقط، بأنه لا يثبت مدعاهم، لأنه إذا تعدد النقلة يمكن أن ينعقد التواتر لعدم اشتراط العدد، وفيه تأمل
The first principle / the book. Ibn al-Hajib [said] that, and the imams of usul such as al-Qadi Abu Bakr and others have explicitly stated the tawatur of all that. And he said: That is correct. And he adduced as evidence what the author indicated by his saying (qila) in the margins of Mirzajan, in agreement with al-Itqan: 'The form (hay'a) is a necessary concomitant of the substance (jawhar), because the substance of the utterance does not exist without it. So when the substance is mutawatir (due to the abundance of motives for transmission, as you have learned), the form becomes necessarily mutawatir.' I say: What is meant by 'type of form' is that which does not vary in the scripts of the mushafs due to differences in qira'at, and the meaning does not vary due to differences in qira'at therein. And it is not among the necessary concomitants. And there is no abundance of motives to transmit details like it, so its tawatur is not obligatory. But this is nothing, because the tawatur was not based on writing in the mushafs, nor for the sake of the meaning, but the abundance of motives necessitated a number that cannot be counted or enumerated, and it is transmitted by memory. In this, the substance and the form are equal, except for what the collective memory of its manner of performance differs, so tawatur of either is not obligatory, like the measurements of prolongation. So the truth accepted by acceptance is this tawatur, and this particularization [mentioned] is an error of Ibn al-Hajib. From this it became clear to you that the criticism of some hadith scholars against the qurra' regarding their refraining from stopping at some places, such as {Say: O disbelievers} [al-Kafirun: 1] — since this contradicts what has been reported about his recitation, peace and blessings be upon him and his family, according to the hadith scholars, and they called stopping at it the recitation of the Prophet — is not in its place. For the refraining that the qurra' practice is also from the Prophet, peace be upon him and his family and companions, so there is no basis for the criticism. Rather, this refraining is mutawatir, and what they have transmitted is khabar ahad. So understand. Then this claim is necessary and does not require proof. Whoever is in doubt should observe the generations, for the transmitters of the seven, rather the ten, qira'at from the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him and his family and companions, until now, at every time their number exceeded the number of the pebbles of al-Batha'. But the author, as a reminder to the heedless, presented the proof and said: For us, if the tawatur of the mentioned qira'at were not [established], then some of the Quran would be non-mutawatir — which is a contradiction. And the entailment is because the particularization (i.e., particularizing some of the qira'at as being Quran to the exclusion of others) is arbitrary (tahakkum), for all have been transmitted equally, and the imams have agreed on the permissibility of praying with them, so all are Quran. The deniers said: The qurra' are seven or less, and this number does not constitute tawatur, so what they agreed upon is not mutawatir — what then of what they differed on? We said: This would only hold if they were the transmitters, which is denied. Rather, the transmitters exceed the number of the pebbles of al-Batha', and their attribution to them is only due to their specializing in verifying them and spending their lives acquiring them, not because they are the sole transmitters. So ponder, for it is clear truth. And it was answered in al-Tahrir by negating the non-constitution of tawatur by this number, for number is not a condition for tawatur. And the author criticized it by saying that a single individual transmits a qira'a, and a single individual is not suitable for constituting tawatur. Perhaps his aim was only to criticize the proof, that it does not establish their claim, because when the transmitters are numerous, tawatur can be constituted due to the absence of a condition of number. In this there is contemplation.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the tawatur (mass transmission) of Quranic readings. The author argues that if the substance (jawhar) of the recitation is mutawatir due to abundant motives for preservation, then the form (hay'a) — that is, the specific manner of performance (such as prolongations) — must also be mutawatir. This is because the form is a necessary concomitant of the substance. The commentator refutes Ibn al-Hajib's objection that the form is not a necessary concomitant and that there is no abundant motive to transmit details. The response is that the transmission was not via writing but through oral memory, and the motives for preservation were abundant for both substance and form, except for minor details like the exact measure of prolongation. The author then uses this to defend the qurra' (reciters) against hadith scholars who criticized them for stopping at certain words, arguing that the reciters' practice is also from the Prophet and mutawatir. Finally, the author refutes deniers who claim that the qurra' are too few to constitute tawatur, stating that the transmitters are in fact countless, and that number is not a condition for tawatur. The passage emphasizes that all accepted qira'at are Quran due to consensus on their permissibility in prayer.

Key Terms
الهيئة (al-hay'a): The specific manner of performance of the recitation, such as prolongation, which does not vary the script or meaning.
الجوهر (al-jawhar): The substance of the utterance, i.e., the letters and words themselves.
التواتر (al-tawatur): Transmission by such a large number that it precludes the possibility of agreement on a falsehood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main basis for the Hanafi argument that the form (hay'a) of qira'at is mutawatir?
A) The form was written in the mus-haf exactly as the substance.
B) The form is a necessary logical concomitant of the mutawatir substance.
C) The form was transmitted by a specific group of seven expert qurra'.
D) The form was established by consensus of later jurists.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the precise manner of recitation (hay'a) is as mutawatir as the words themselves due to their inseparable connection and the abundant oral preservation.

The Authority of Irregular Quranic Readings
Disputing the authority of irregular Quranic readings as a source of law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi argument that irregular Quranic readings are hujja and contrast it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the key usul principle ('hearing from the Prophet' vs 'tawatur/report format').

Core Idea
Irregular readings are hujja because they are heard from the Prophet, even if not mutawatir.

In this passage, the author defends the Hanafi position that irregular Quranic readings (al-qira'at al-shadhdha) are authoritative legal proofs. The central debate is whether a reading transmitted by a single trustworthy Companion, but not meeting the conditions of tawatur or formal report classification, can be used to derive rulings. The Hanafi school asserts that the mere fact of hearing from the Prophet suffices for legal obligation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi claim
Identify the Hanafi position: irregular readings are hujja because they are heard from the Prophet through a trustworthy chain.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i argue that such readings are neither mutawatir (so not Quran) nor transmitted as separate reports (so not khabar), thus not binding.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The condition for action is hearing from the Prophet, not a specific form of transmission. The companion's trustworthy report is sufficient.
Key point: 'hearing' is the operative element.
4
Examine the counter-argument about error
Even if the companion mistakenly described the transmission as Quran, the fact of hearing remains; the error does not negate the report.
The author refutes the claim that the attribution is erroneous.
5
Conclude with the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis can use such readings to derive rulings (e.g., consecutive fasting), while Shafi'is cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنه (بقراءة ابن مسعود) فصيام ثلاثة أيام متتابعات، وذكر الرافعي من كبار أصحابه والقاضي أبو الطيب الحسين أن مذهبه العمل به كخبر الواحد وصححه السبكي في جمع الجوامع و شرح المختصر، وقد احتج بعض أصحابه على قطع يمين السارق بقراءة ابن مسعود مع أنها من الشواذ كذا في الإتقان»، وقال فيه : وإنما لم يحتج أصحابنا بقراءة متتابعات لادعائهم النسخ (لنا) أنه مسموع عن النبي عليه وأصحابه وآله الصلاة والسلام) روی عدل جازم (وكل ما كان مسموعاً عنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فهو حجة) لما أنه لا ينطق عن الهوى، وأما الظنية فلأنه يعد من الآحاد (و) لنا (أيضاً) أنه إما) قرآن أو خبر) لأن نقل العدل لا سيما مقطوع العدالة كأصحاب بدر وبيعة الرضوان لا يكون من اختراع بل سماع، فهو إما قرآن قد نسخ تلاوته، أو خبر وقع تفسيراً ، فهو قرآن أو خبر وكل منهما يجب العمل به) فإن قلت : الخصم لا يسلم الانحصار، بل يجوّز كونه مذهب الراوي، فنقله قرآناً؟ قال : (وتجويز كونه مذهباً له فنقله قرآنا عجب ليس للمسلم أن يجترى عليه لأن الصحابي العادل بل مقطوع العدالة كيف يفعل هذا الأمر الشنيع؟ وفي حواشي ميرزاجان» أن العجب إنما يصح لو كان مراد الخصم أن مدلوله كان مذهباً له، فنقله قرآناً للترويج، فإنه لا شك أنه لا يتأتى من آحاد العدول الصحابة، بل مراده لعله كان قرآنيته مذهباً بالاجتهاد فنقل على ما كان مذهباً له، ومذهب الراوي غير حجة، سيما إذا ظهر خطؤه بيقين وهذا مما لا عجب فيه . وجوابه : أن القرآنية مما لا يهتدي إليها الرأي ولا مدخل له فيه، فاتخاذ الصحابي العادل مذهباً لا بد له من سماع، فإما كان قرآناً فنسخت تلاوته ولم يطلع هو عليه كما هو الأولى، أو وقع تفسيراً فظنه حين السماع قرآناً، وعلى كل تقدير فهو حجة، وهذا معنى الترديد المذكور. الشافعي (قالوا) إنه ليس بقرآن، إذ لا تواتر وما ليس بمتواتر ليس قرآناً ولا خبر يصح العمل به، إذ لم ينقل خبراً، وهو شرط صحة العمل) فلا يصح العمل بدونه (قلنا) كون النقل خبراً شرط صحة العمل (ممنوع، بل الشرط السماع عنه صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم مطلقاً) والإجماع إنما هو على أن الخبر الذي لم ينسب إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لا يجب به العمل، وهذا قد نسب إليه، لأنه نقل قرآناً هذا، لكن لقائل أن يقول : إن النسبة التي نسب بها خطأ قطعاً، فلم تبق وليس هناك نسبة أخرى، فبقي الخبر من غير نسبة بالسماع، ويستعان لدفعه بما سبق من أن أصل السماع مقطوع، والتوصيف بالقرآنية وإن كان مقطوع الخطأ لكن ببطلانه لا يبطل نفسه السماع هذا.
Because (by the reading of Ibn Mas'ud) it is fasting three consecutive days, and al-Rafi'i among his major companions and Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Husayn said that his madhhab is to act upon it like a solitary report, and al-Subki authenticated it in Jam' al-Jawami' and Sharh al-Mukhtasar. Some of his companions argued for cutting the thief's hand by the reading of Ibn Mas'ud even though it is from the irregular readings, as in al-Itqan. He said therein: Our companions only did not argue with the reading of 'consecutive' due to their claim of abrogation. (For us) it is heard from the Prophet (peace be upon him and his Companions and Family) narrated by a decisive trustworthy person, and everything heard from him (peace be upon him and his Companions and Family) is a proof, because he does not speak from desire. As for its being conjectural, it is considered from solitary reports. (And) for us (also) it is either Quran or report, because the transmission of a trustworthy person, especially one of definitive justice like the Companions of Badr and the Pledge of Ridwan, cannot be invented but is heard. So it is either Quran whose recitation has been abrogated, or a report that occurred as an interpretation. So it is either Quran or report, and each of them must be acted upon. If you say: The opponent does not concede the exclusivity, rather he allows it to be the madhhab of the narrator, then he transmitted it as Quran? He said: (And allowing it to be his madhhab and then transmitting it as Quran is astonishing; a Muslim should not dare to do that, because the trustworthy companion, rather one of definitive justice, how would he do this heinous act? And in the footnotes of Mirzajan: That astonishment would only be valid if the opponent meant that its meaning was his madhhab, so he transmitted it as Quran for promotion – no doubt that cannot come from individual trustworthy companions. Rather his meaning perhaps was that its being Quran was his madhhab by ijtihad, so he transmitted according to what was his madhhab. The madhhab of the narrator is not a proof, especially if his error is known with certainty, and this has no astonishment. And its answer: That being Quran cannot be reached by opinion nor does opinion have any entry in it. So the trustworthy companion adopting it as a madhhab must have hearing. So either it was Quran and its recitation was abrogated and he was not aware of it, as is more appropriate, or it occurred as interpretation and he thought it was Quran at the time of hearing. In either case, it is a proof. This is the meaning of the aforementioned alternation. (Al-Shafi'i) They said: It is not Quran, because there is no tawatur, and what is not mutawatir is not Quran, nor is it a report that can be acted upon, because it was not transmitted as a report, and that is a condition for the validity of acting upon it. So it is not valid to act without it. (We said) That transmission as a report being a condition for validity of action is denied. Rather the condition is hearing from him (peace be upon him and his Family and Companions) absolutely. Consensus is only that a report that is not attributed to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his Companions and Family) is not obligatory to act upon. And this one has been attributed to him because it was transmitted as Quran. But one might say: The attribution by which it was attributed is definitely erroneous, so it remains without attribution, and there is no other attribution. So the report remains without attribution by hearing, and to repel this one resorts to what preceded that the basis of hearing is definitive, and the description of being Quran, even if its error is definitive, but its invalidity does not invalidate the hearing itself. This.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a dispute regarding the authority of irregular Quranic readings (qira'at shadhdha). The Hanafi position is that such readings are hujja (proof) because they are heard from the Prophet (saw) through a reliable chain, even if not mutawatir. The author argues that the transmission from a trustworthy companion must be based on hearing, so it is either an abrogated Quranic verse or an explanatory report; both are binding. The Shafi'i objection that it lacks tawatur and is not transmitted as a separate report is refuted: the condition for action is hearing from the Prophet, not a specific form of transmission. The passage then addresses a subtle counter: if the companion mistakenly attributed his own opinion as Quran, the hearing is still proven, and the error in description does not negate the fact of hearing. Thus, the irregular reading remains a valid proof. The discussion shows the Hanafi reliance on the principle that trustworthy transmission from the Prophet is sufficient for legal obligation, even if it does not meet the strict conditions for Quranic status.

Key Terms
القراءة الشاذة (al-qira'at al-shadhdha): A Quranic reading that is not mutawatir but transmitted through a non-tawatur chain.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what makes an irregular Quranic reading legally binding?
A) Its tawatur (mass transmission)
B) Its transmission as a separate report
C) Its being heard from the Prophet through a trustworthy chain
D) Its inclusion in the official Mushaf

Key Takeaway
The authority of irregular Quranic readings rests on the fact that they are heard from the Prophet through trustworthy transmission, regardless of their categorization as Quran or report.

The Meaning of Mutashabihat: A Usul Dispute on Quranic Interpretation
Dispute over whether mutashabihat are known only to Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on mutashabihat, apply the linguistic argument of waqf and istinaf from Quran 3:7, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Mutashabihat verses are known only to Allah; the firmly grounded affirm faith without interpretation.

This passage presents one of the most enduring usul disputes: do the ambiguous verses of the Quran (mutashabihat) have an interpretation known to anyone besides Allah? The Hanafi school, following the Salaf, maintains that their true meaning is known only to Allah, while some later scholars (attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i) claim that all Quran is understood by some. The author defends the Hanafi position with a careful linguistic analysis of Quran 3:7, focusing on the rule of pausing (waqf) and the grammatical structure of the verse. Understanding this dispute is crucial for usul al-fiqh because it determines the methodology of tafsir and the limits of human interpretation of divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and Two Positions
State the central question: Do the mutashabihat verses have an interpretation known to anyone besides Allah? Identify the Hanafi/Salaf position (only Allah knows) and the opposing view (some scholars know, attributed to al-Shafi'i).
The Hanafi view is that even the Prophet (s) may have known, but the passage focuses on scholars after him.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Proof: The Waqf Rule
Examine the Hanafi reliance on the necessary stop (waqf lazim) after 'illa Allah' in Quran 3:7. Explain how this prevents the coordination of 'wa al-rasikhun' with Allah, making it a new sentence (istinaf).
The author cites all reciters' agreement on this waqf.
3
Examine the Opposing Shafi'i Claim and Its Basis
The opposing view holds that 'wa al-rasikhun' is conjoined to Allah, implying that the firmly grounded also know the interpretation. This is supported by reports from Ibn Abbas and others that they knew the ta'wil.
The author mentions these reports but then refutes them.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response and the Author's Tarjih
The Hanafi response uses the readings of Ibn Mas'ud, Ubayy, and Ibn Abbas that show 'wa al-rasikhun' as a new beginning (istinaf). The author also argues from context: the deviators seek ta'wil, so the firmly grounded must have the opposite share, i.e., not seeking it. The author concludes that the Salaf position is 'more fitting and correct'.
He also notes that irregular readings do not provide certainty for creedal matters but can support the practical ruling.

Issue: In it is that which is not understood by anyone, and Allah has exclusively kept its knowledge. The two Imams Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma specified the issue as excluding the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his Companions and Family), and it is more fitting and correct. How could it not be, and addressing with that which the addressee does not understand is not befitting to His majesty, exalted. (It is the madhhab of the Salaf from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. (And it is said) among their later ones: All of it is understood by some, attributing to Imam al-Shafi'i.
