Usul Dispute: One Tawaf or Two for the Qarin? Bayan, Qawl, and Fi'l in Conflict
Usul dispute on conflict between qawl and fi'l in determining the rites of qarin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of tarjih between conflicting qawl and fi'l to evaluate the dispute on the number of tawaf for the qarin.

Core Idea
When qawl and fi'l contradict, preference is given to the fi'l if supported by stronger narrators and contextual evidence.

This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is on the number of tawaf and sa'i for a qarin. At its core, it is a struggle between a hadith qawli (statement) and a hadith fi'li (action), and the principles of bayan and tarjih. We will dissect the arguments and see how the Hanafi school weighs evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the exact disagreement: does the qarin perform two tawafs and two sa'is (one set for each) or one combined set?
Hanafis say two; Shafi'is say one.
2
Map the proofs
List the primary evidence for each side: Shafi'i relies on the qawl of Ibn 'Umar (marfu') and the statement 'Umrah entered into Hajj'. Hanafis rely on the fi'l of 'Ali, the endorsement of 'Umar, and the Quranic verse 2:196.
Also note the usul classification: fi'l vs qawl.
3
Analyze the usul principle of bayan
Understand the Shafi'i argument that qawl is the stronger bayan (clarification) because it is explicit. The Hanafi response is that fi'l can be preferred when it comes from more reliable narrators and is supported by other evidences.
The principle of 'al-qawl huwa al-bayan' is contested here.
4
Apply the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school gives preference to the fi'l because the narrators ('Ali, 'Umar, Ibn Mas'ud) are considered stronger in precision and fiqh than Ibn 'Umar alone. Also, the fi'l is supported by qiyas and the Quran.
Tarjih is based on narrator strength and supporting evidence.
5
Consider the Quranic evidence
The Hanafis use the Quranic command 'complete the Hajj and Umrah' as a decisive proof that each worship has its own complete rites, which cannot be overridden by a khabar wahid.
This is a final, strong argument that settles the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة اختلفوا في أن القارن عليه طوافان وسعيان للعمرة والحج أو واحد لهما، فإمامنا وصاحباه ذهبوا إلى الأول والشافعي إلى الثاني، واستدل بما مر عن رواية الترمذي، وبقوله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام : دخلت العمرة في الحج واستدلوا لنا بما مر من حديث أمير المؤمنين علي فأوردوا أنه نقل فعل وحديث ابن عمر نقل قول، والقول هو البيان فإن قلت : كشفنا عنك الغطاء وبينا أنه لا وجه لبيانية القول قلت : إنما كشفت الغطاء فيما يعلم القبلية للفعل، وهي ههنا مجهولة بعد وأجاب عنه المصنف ناقلاً عن التقرير أن القول إنما يتعين للبيانية إذا لم يدل دليل على قوة الفعل وترجيحه وههنا قد دل، وهو قول أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه لمن طاف طوافين وسعى سعيين : هديت لسنة نبيك هذا، وهذا الحديث رواه الإمام أبو حنيفة عن صبي بن معبد في قصة طويلة، فإن قلت: قد روي هذا الحديث وليس فيه ذكر الطوافين إنما أخبر صبي بالقران فأجاب أمير المؤمنين بما ذكر ففيه اضطراب؟ قلت كلا فإن زيادة الثقة مقبولة، كيف وليس في الروايات الأخر ما ينافيه، بل هذا مبين للروايات الأخر وكاشف لإجمالها ، لكن هذا غير وافٍ كما لا يخفى على المتأمل، فإن فعل أمير المؤمنين عمر إنما حكم بهداية السنة وموافقتها، وهذا لا يدل على الوجوب أما عند الخصم فظاهر لأن السنة المطلقة عنده تحمل على فعل الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وعندنا على الطريقة في الدين وهو يشمل الواجب والمندوب والمواظب عليه، بل نقل الفعلان أيضاً متعارضين فإنه روى الشيخان عن ابن عمر أنه قرن فطاف لهما طوافاً واحداً وقال : وهكذا فعل رسول الله فالحق إذن أن الفعلين قد تعارضا، والقول وافق أحدهما، فإذن توجه بأن الترجيح في مثله للقول فإن قلت الفعلان لا يتعارضان؟ قلت : ههنا علم التعارض من خارج، فإن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لم يحج بعد الهجرة إلا مرة واحدة فإن كان نسكه قراناً كما نطق به أكثر الروايات فهو في حجة الوداع لا غير، وقد نقل الفعلان فقد تعارضا ،البتة وإنما يتعارضان إذا احتمل التعدد، وقد رجح أصحابنا فعل الطوافين بأن رواية أمير المؤمنين عمر وأمير المؤمنين علي رضي الله عنهما، أرجح على رواية ابن عمر فإنهما راجحان في الضبط والاتقان والفقاهة، مع أن هذا مذهبهما ومذهب عبد الله بن مسعود ومذهب عمران بن الحصين رضي الله تعالى عنهم، وهم أرجحون على ابن عمر وأيضاً قد اعتضد هذا بالقياس فإن ضم عبادة إلى عبادة لا يوجب نقصاً في أركان أحدهما، كيف وإذا ضم شفع نفل إلى شفع في التحريمة لا يتداخل شيء من أركان أحدهما في الآخر، مع أن الاحتياط في العبادات يقتضي ذلك أيضاً، والحق في الاستدلال عند هذا العبد أن يستدل بقوله تعالى : ﴿وَأَتِمُوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٩٦] فهذا يدل بالعبارة على أن إتمام أركان كل واجب فإن معناه : ائتوهما ،تامين فلا يعارضه خبر الواحد لا سيما الذي حكم بغرابته فيتأول بأنه أجزأه طواف واحد لكل منهما طواف للعمرة وطواف للحج، ويكون الإشارة إلى أن طوافي القدوم والوداع ليسا ركنين فافهم.
،
،
وأما الجواب : عن الثاني فبأن الحديث محمول على القرآن لا على أن العمرة، ذهب من البين وقام طواف الحج مقامهما فافهم.
Benefit: They differed on whether the qarin has two tawafs and two sa'is for Umrah and Hajj, or one for both. Our Imam and his two companions went to the first, and al-Shafi'i to the second. He argued with what was mentioned from the narration of al-Tirmidhi, and with his statement (peace be upon him and his family and companions): 'Umrah has entered into Hajj.' And they argued for us with what was mentioned from the hadith of the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali. So it was objected that he narrated an action, and the hadith of Ibn 'Umar narrated a statement, and the statement is the bayan. If you say: We have uncovered the covering and explained that there is no basis for the bayan of the statement. I say: You have only uncovered the covering regarding what is known to be prior to the action, and here it is still unknown. And the author answered, quoting from al-Taqrir, that the statement is determined for bayan only if there is no evidence for the strength and preference of the action, and here there is, namely the statement of the Commander of the Faithful 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) to the one who performed two tawafs and two sa'is: 'You have been guided to the Sunnah of your Prophet.' This hadith was narrated by Imam Abu Hanifa from Subay' ibn Ma'bad in a lengthy story. If you say: This hadith has been narrated and does not mention the two tawafs; he only informed Subay' about qiran, and the Commander of the Faithful responded as mentioned, so there is confusion. I say: No, for the addition of a trustworthy narrator is accepted. Moreover, there is no contradiction in other narrations. Rather, this clarifies the other narrations and removes their ambiguity. But this is insufficient, as is not hidden from the thoughtful one. Indeed, the action of the Commander of the Faithful 'Umar only judged guidance to the Sunnah and its conformity. This does not indicate obligation. As for the opponent, it is apparent because the absolute Sunnah with him is carried on the action of the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family and companions). With us, it is on the way in the religion, which includes obligatory, recommended, and those he persevered upon. Rather, the two actions are also contradictory. For the two shaykhs narrated from Ibn 'Umar that he performed qiran and performed one tawaf for both, and said: 'Thus the Messenger of Allah did.' So the truth then is that the two actions are contradictory, and the statement agreed with one of them. So it is directed that preference in such a case is for the statement. If you say: The two actions do not contradict? I say: Here contradiction is known externally. Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) only performed Hajj once after the Hijrah. If his pilgrimage was qiran as most narrations state, then it was only in the Farewell Pilgrimage. And two actions have been narrated, so they absolutely contradict. They only contradict if multiplicity is possible. Our companions preferred the action of two tawafs because the narration of the Commander of the Faithful 'Umar and the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them) is stronger than the narration of Ibn 'Umar, for they are superior in precision, accuracy, and fiqh. Moreover, this is their madhhab and the madhhab of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and 'Imran ibn Husayn (may Allah be pleased with them), and they are stronger than Ibn 'Umar. Also, this is supported by qiyas, for adding one worship to another does not cause deficiency in the pillars of either. How, when one adds a supererogatory pair to a pair in the tahrima, none of the pillars of one enters the other. Moreover, caution in acts of worship also requires that. The truth in istidlal according to this servant is to use the statement of Allah Most High: {And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah} (al-Baqarah 2:196). This indicates by explicit wording that the pillars of each are obligatory, meaning: perform them complete. So a khabar al-wahid does not oppose it, especially one ruled as ghareeb. So it is interpreted that 'one tawaf sufficed him' means one tawaf for each, a tawaf for Umrah and a tawaf for Hajj, and the reference is that the tawaf of arrival and the tawaf of farewell are not pillars. So understand.

As for the answer to the second, it is that the hadith is interpreted as referring to qiran, not that Umrah has disappeared and the tawaf of Hajj takes its place. So understand.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a fiqhi-usuli dispute about the number of tawaf and sa'i for a qarin (one combining Hajj and Umrah). The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that the qarin must perform two separate tawafs and two sa'is—one for Umrah, one for Hajj. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one tawaf and one sa'i suffice for both, relying on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar (marfu') and the Prophet's statement 'Umrah has entered into Hajj.' The Hanafis rely on the action of 'Ali (and the Prophet) narrated by Ibn al-Hanafiyya, and the endorsement of 'Umar. The author analyzes the usul principle: the qawl (statement) of Ibn 'Umar is a hadith qawli, while the fi'l (action) of 'Ali is a hadith fi'li. Since statement is generally preferred as bayan, but here the action is supported by the statement of 'Umar and the qarin's own practice of the Companions. He also discusses contradiction between the two actions (one tawaf vs. two) and resolves it by weighing narrators: 'Ali and 'Umar are stronger than Ibn 'Umar. He also uses the Quranic verse (2:196) 'complete the Hajj and Umrah' as evidence that each has its own complete rites, and a khabar al-wahid cannot override it. The hadith of one tawaf is interpreted to mean one tawaf for each (combined intention) or that the extra tawafs (arrival/departure) are not pillars. The Hanafi position is thus supported by stronger narrators, qiyas, and the Quran.

Key Terms
القارن (al-qarin): من جمع بين الحج والعمرة في إحرام واحد
البيان (al-bayan): الإيضاح للمجمل، وفي هذا السياق: القول أو الفعل الذي يوضح حكم المجمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, how many tawafs must a qarin perform?
A) One tawaf for both Hajj and Umrah combined.
B) Two tawafs: one for Umrah and one for Hajj.
C) Three tawafs: one for Umrah, one for Hajj, and one for farewell.
D) No tawaf is required; only sa'i is needed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a qarin must perform two separate tawafs and two sa'is, based on the Quran, stronger narrators, and qiyas, despite the Shafi'i reliance on the qawl of Ibn 'Umar.

Consensus and Quranic Abrogation: Distinguishing Naskh from Takhsis
Introduction of a Quranic proof by those who allow naskh by ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the claim that consensus can abrogate a Quranic text by identifying the textual category and applying Hanafi principles to distinguish naskh from takhsis.

Core Idea
What appears as naskh by ijma is actually takhsis — the Quranic text remains authoritative; consensus clarifies its application.

In this passage, those who argue that consensus (ijma) can abrogate (naskh) a Quranic ruling cite the verse on inheritance shares (4:11). They claim that the Companions' consensus effectively altered the literal meaning. A Hanafi usuli must carefully distinguish between true naskh — lifting a ruling — and mere specification (takhsis) or interpretation. The key is to examine the textual category and the role of consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and evidence
Recognize that the opponent uses the Companions' consensus on Quran 4:11 as proof that ijma can abrogate. Note the verse and the narration of Ibn Abbas.
The opponent's argument is based on one specific case.
2
Classify the textual category of the verse
Determine that the verse (4:11) is a zahir — its apparent meaning gives the mother one-sixth when siblings exist. In Hanafi usul, zahir is binding unless there is a contrary proof.
Zahir is not mutlak; it can be specified.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul rule
The rule: A text remains authoritative until abrogated by equally strong evidence (Quran or mutawatir sunnah). Consensus is not a source of naskh; it can only clarify or specify.
Hanafis require a clear textual source for naskh.
4
Distinguish naskh from takhsis
Explain that the Company's consensus did not lift the ruling but specified its conditions. This is takhsis, not naskh. The verse still applies; its scope is refined.
Confusing the two leads to incorrect usul methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجيزو ناسخية الإجماع (قالوا أولاً) حين سأل ابن عباس قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ ﴾ [النساء: ١١]
Those who permit the abrogating property of consensus: (They said first) When Ibn Abbas asked, Allah Almighty said: {But if he has siblings, then for his mother the sixth} [al-Nisa 4:11].
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This short passage quotes the opening of an argument by those who claim that consensus (ijma) can abrogate (naskh). They cite a narration: when Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) asked about the interpretation of Quran 4:11 regarding inheritance shares for siblings, the verse was understood to have been abrogated by the consensus of the Companions on a different ruling. This is presented as evidence that ijma can function as a naskh. The author ('fawatih al-rahmat') is here reporting the opponent's argument before responding. The verse itself is from Surah al-Nisa, stating: 'But if he has brothers, then for his mother the sixth' – which deals with inheritance shares. The opponent likely argues that the Companions' consensus on a different distribution abrogated the literal meaning.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation – the lifting of a ruling. Here used by opponents to argue consensus can abrogate.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of mujtahidun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the proper classification of the Companions' consensus regarding Quran 4:11?
A) Naskh (abrogation)
B) Takhsis (specification)
C) Ijtihad (independent reasoning)
D) Bid'ah (innovation)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between naskh and takhsis is essential: a verse remains authoritative unless abrogated by equally strong evidence; consensus only specifies its application.

Hanafi Classification of Reports by Certainty of Truth
Classification of reports by epistemic certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the Hanafi classification of reports (khabar) into five categories based on how truth or falsehood is known: by necessity, by reasoning, by presumption, equal probability, and the corrected Hanafi position on the unknown narrator.

Core Idea
A report's truth value is not binary: Hanafi usul recognizes grades from certain true through probable to possible falsehood.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut lays out the Hanafi taxonomy of reports by epistemic certainty. Understanding this classification is essential for evaluating hadith and other sources of evidence in fiqh. The author distinguishes between reports known true by necessity, by reasoning, and those that are merely probable, addressing a common misconception that unknown narrators yield equal probability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary categories of certain truth
List the three ways a report can be known true with certainty: by necessity in itself (mutawatir), by necessity through something else (mathematical truths), and by reasoning (reports of Allah/Messenger). Note the special case of those who witness directly.
The passage also includes reports of ahl al-ijma' in certainties under reasoned knowledge.
2
Examine the category of reports not known true with certainty
The passage lists solitary reports with circumstantial evidence (may yield knowledge if sufficient), then the categories of conjecture: just narrator (probable true), habitual liar (probable false), and unknown narrator (initially said equal but corrected).
The author objects to the 'equal' classification for majhul because Hanafi school accepts his testimony and narration as proof.
3
Analyze the objection to the 'equal probability' claim
The author argues that the unknown narrator's report is actually maznun al-sidq (presumed true) with weak presumption, based on the Hanafi acceptance of his testimony and narration in non-zahir al-riwayah.
This shows the school's internal refinement of a general statement.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah)
The classification determines whether a report can be used as evidence: certain reports are qat'i, probable reports are zanni and may be subject to further scrutiny. The unknown narrator's report, though weak, is still accepted as proof in some contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً : الخبر إما يعلم صدقه ضرورة بنفسه وهو المتواتر أو يعلم صدقه ضرورة بغيره وهو الموافق للعلم الضروري الذي علم به سواء أخبر أم لا مثل الواحد نصف الاثنين فإنه علم مضمونه ضرورة سواء أخبر أم لا أو يعلم صدقه نظراً كخبر الله تعالى والرسول فإنه يعلم صدقه بتوسط أن الخبر صادر عن الله ورسوله وكل ما صدر عنهما فهو صادق، وهذا لمن لم يبلغ مقام المشاهدة والحدس وأما من بلغ إلى حد هذين المقامين فهو معلوم الصدق ضرورة وخبر أهل الإجماع الموافق للنظر الصحيح في القطعيات كالهندسيات والحسابيات، وعلى هذا يخرج خبر الواحد المحفوف بالقرائن فيرد أشكال اختلال الحصر عند من يراه مفيداً للعلم إلا أن يدخل فيما يفيد العلم نظراً أو يعلم كذبه ضرورة أو نظراً وهو كل خبر مخالف أي مناف لما علم صدقه أو لا يعلم شيء منهما أي الصدق والكذب فقد يظن أحدهما كخبر الواحد العدل فإنه مظنون مع احتمال السهو والنسيان وخبر الواحد الكذوب فإنه يظن كذبه مع احتمال الصدق، فإن الكذوب قد يصدق وقد يتساويان صدقاً وكذباً كالمجهول أي كخبر الواحد المجهول العدالة والكذب، كذا قالوا، لكن يرد عليه أن خبره حجة عند البعض بل شهادته مقبولة عند الإمام الهمام رضي الله تعالى عنه، بل روايته أيضاً على ما روى عنه في غير ظاهر الرواية مقبولة، فكيف يكون خبره متساوياً صدقاً وكذباً، بل يكون مظنون الصدق غاية الأمر الظن ضعيف وقال بعض الظاهرية : كل ما لا يعلم صدقه يعلم كذبه والظاهر ما نقلوا عنهم أنهم أرادوا به الجزم المطابق كخبر مدعي الرسالة أي أنهم قاسوا على خبر مدعي الرسالة فإنه متى لم يعلم صدقه بإراءة المعجزات يجزم بالكذب فإن الإخبار سواسية وهو أي قول الظاهرية باطل لاستلزامه ارتفاع النقيضين المستلزم لاجتماعهما لأن كذب كل ملزوم صدق الآخر فكذبهما ملزوم صدقهما، ولا استحالة في العلاقة بين مستحيل ومنافيه بل هو الحق على ما تنادى عليه الأقيسة الخلفية
Additionally: a report is either known to be true by necessity in itself, and that is the mutawatir; or known to be true by necessity through something else, and that is what agrees with necessary knowledge known regardless of whether it is reported or not, like 'one is half of two', for its content is known necessarily whether reported or not; or known to be true by reasoning, like the report of Allah and the Messenger, for its truth is known through the mediation that the report originates from Allah and His Messenger, and everything that originates from them is true. This is for one who has not reached the station of witnessing and intuition; as for one who has reached that station, it is known to be true by necessity. And the report of the people of consensus that agrees with sound reasoning in certainties like geometrical and arithmetical matters. Based on this, the solitary report accompanied by circumstantial evidence is excluded, so the problem of incompleteness of the classification arises for those who consider it useful for knowledge, unless it enters into what yields knowledge by reasoning or is known to be false by necessity or reasoning. And it is every report that contradicts [what is known to be true] or nothing is known of either [truth or falsehood]. Then one of them may be presumed, like the solitary report of a just narrator, for it is presumed [true] with the possibility of forgetfulness and oversight, and the solitary report of a habitual liar, for its falsehood is presumed with the possibility of truth, for a liar may sometimes tell the truth. And they may be equal in truth and falsehood, like the unknown [narrator], i.e., the solitary report of one whose justice and lying are unknown. This is what they said. But one may object that his report is proof according to some, indeed his testimony is accepted by the great Imam (may Allah be pleased with him), and his narration is also accepted according to what is reported from him in non-zahir al-riwayah, so how can his report be equal in truth and falsehood? Rather, it is presumed true, but the presumption is weak. Some of the Zahiriyya said: everything whose truth is not known, its falsehood is known. The apparent meaning is that they intended by it the certain matching [of reality], like the report of a claimant to prophethood. That is, they analogized to the report of a claimant to prophethood, for when his truth is not known through showing miracles, one is certain of his falsehood, because reports are equal. And this, i.e., the statement of the Zahiriyya, is false because it entails the negation of both contradictories, which necessitates their conjunction, because the falsehood of each necessitates the truth of the other, so the falsehood of both necessitates their truth. And there is no impossibility in the relationship between the impossible and its negation, rather it is the truth according to the well-known reductio ad absurdum arguments.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a classification of reports (akhbar) based on how we know their truth or falsehood. The author presents a Hanafi usul taxonomy: first, reports known true by necessity in themselves (mutawatir); second, reports known true by necessity through something else (like mathematical truths); third, reports known true by reasoning (like reports from Allah and the Messenger). For those who have reached spiritual realization, such reports are known by necessity. The report of the people of consensus (ahl al-ijma') in certainties also falls under reasoned knowledge. The classification then covers reports that are not known true with certainty: solitary reports with circumstantial evidence may yield knowledge if they are accompanied by enough indications. For reports that do not yield certainty, they fall into conjecture: the report of a just narrator is probable (maznun al-sidq), that of a habitual liar is probable falsehood, and that of an unknown narrator was said to be equal in probability, but the author objects that in the Hanafi school, such a report is still considered proof and thus is more likely true, albeit with weak probability. The author then refutes the Zahiriyya position that every report not known true is known false, using a reductio argument: if two unknown narrators report contradictory statements, and neither is known true, then according to the Zahiriyya both would be known false, leading to both contradictories being false, which is impossible. Therefore the Zahiriyya position is invalid. The Hanafi position is that reports are classified by levels of certainty, with a middle ground of probability.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report or statement conveying information.
صدق (sidq): A report matching reality (al-waqi').
كذب (kidhb): A report not matching reality.
ضرورة (darura): Knowledge that is immediate and unavoidable, without need for reasoning.
نظر (nazar): Knowledge obtained through reasoning and inference.
مظنون (maznun): Something that is presumed or probable, based on conjecture (zann).
مجهول (majhul): An unknown narrator whose justice and lying are not known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, the report that 'one is half of two' falls under which category?
A) Known true by necessity in itself (mutawatir)
B) Known true by necessity through something else
C) Known true by reasoning
D) Known false

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of reports balances certainty and probability, with the unknown narrator's report considered weakly presumed true due to its acceptance as proof in the school.

8 min
Refuting the Zahiriyya: Not Known True Does Not Imply False
Refutation of the Zahiriyya claim using logical argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Zahiriyya position that 'every report not known true is known false' using the Hanafi reductio argument from the passage.

Core Idea
The Zahiriyya claim leads to logical absurdity: if two unknown narrators give opposite reports, both would be false, which is impossible.

In this passage, after laying out the Hanafi classification, the author refutes a radical position held by some Zahiriyya scholars: that any report whose truth is not known must be known false. This is a classic example of using rational argument (dalil aqli) to defend the Hanafi usul against an extreme view. The author employs a reductio ad absurdum (qiyas khalfi) to show the flaw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Zahiriyya claim
The Zahiriyya are reported to say: 'Everything whose truth is not known, its falsehood is known.' They analogize to the case of a claimant to prophethood: if his truth is not shown by miracles, we know he is false.
This is a strong claim that everything non-certain is false.
2
Understand the Hanafi reductio argument
If we have two unknown narrators giving contradictory reports (one says X, the other says not-X), and neither report is known true, then according to the Zahiriyya both would be known false. But if both are false, then both X and not-X are false, which means they are both false, but one must be true (since they are contradictories). Therefore the Zahiriyya position leads to the impossibility of both contradictories being false.
The logical form: assume both reports are false => both X and not-X are false => violation of law of excluded middle.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the Zahiriyya view were accepted, then all reports from unknown narrators would be rejected outright, which is too extreme. The Hanafi view allows for graded acceptance based on probability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً : الخبر إما يعلم صدقه ضرورة بنفسه وهو المتواتر أو يعلم صدقه ضرورة بغيره وهو الموافق للعلم الضروري الذي علم به سواء أخبر أم لا مثل الواحد نصف الاثنين فإنه علم مضمونه ضرورة سواء أخبر أم لا أو يعلم صدقه نظراً كخبر الله تعالى والرسول فإنه يعلم صدقه بتوسط أن الخبر صادر عن الله ورسوله وكل ما صدر عنهما فهو صادق، وهذا لمن لم يبلغ مقام المشاهدة والحدس وأما من بلغ إلى حد هذين المقامين فهو معلوم الصدق ضرورة وخبر أهل الإجماع الموافق للنظر الصحيح في القطعيات كالهندسيات والحسابيات، وعلى هذا يخرج خبر الواحد المحفوف بالقرائن فيرد أشكال اختلال الحصر عند من يراه مفيداً للعلم إلا أن يدخل فيما يفيد العلم نظراً أو يعلم كذبه ضرورة أو نظراً وهو كل خبر مخالف أي مناف لما علم صدقه أو لا يعلم شيء منهما أي الصدق والكذب فقد يظن أحدهما كخبر الواحد العدل فإنه مظنون مع احتمال السهو والنسيان وخبر الواحد الكذوب فإنه يظن كذبه مع احتمال الصدق، فإن الكذوب قد يصدق وقد يتساويان صدقاً وكذباً كالمجهول أي كخبر الواحد المجهول العدالة والكذب، كذا قالوا، لكن يرد عليه أن خبره حجة عند البعض بل شهادته مقبولة عند الإمام الهمام رضي الله تعالى عنه، بل روايته أيضاً على ما روى عنه في غير ظاهر الرواية مقبولة، فكيف يكون خبره متساوياً صدقاً وكذباً، بل يكون مظنون الصدق غاية الأمر الظن ضعيف وقال بعض الظاهرية : كل ما لا يعلم صدقه يعلم كذبه والظاهر ما نقلوا عنهم أنهم أرادوا به الجزم المطابق كخبر مدعي الرسالة أي أنهم قاسوا على خبر مدعي الرسالة فإنه متى لم يعلم صدقه بإراءة المعجزات يجزم بالكذب فإن الإخبار سواسية وهو أي قول الظاهرية باطل لاستلزامه ارتفاع النقيضين المستلزم لاجتماعهما لأن كذب كل ملزوم صدق الآخر فكذبهما ملزوم صدقهما، ولا استحالة في العلاقة بين مستحيل ومنافيه بل هو الحق على ما تنادى عليه الأقيسة الخلفية
Additionally: a report is either known to be true by necessity in itself, and that is the mutawatir; or known to be true by necessity through something else, and that is what agrees with necessary knowledge known regardless of whether it is reported or not, like 'one is half of two', for its content is known necessarily whether reported or not; or known to be true by reasoning, like the report of Allah and the Messenger, for its truth is known through the mediation that the report originates from Allah and His Messenger, and everything that originates from them is true. This is for one who has not reached the station of witnessing and intuition; as for one who has reached that station, it is known to be true by necessity. And the report of the people of consensus that agrees with sound reasoning in certainties like geometrical and arithmetical matters. Based on this, the solitary report accompanied by circumstantial evidence is excluded, so the problem of incompleteness of the classification arises for those who consider it useful for knowledge, unless it enters into what yields knowledge by reasoning or is known to be false by necessity or reasoning. And it is every report that contradicts [what is known to be true] or nothing is known of either [truth or falsehood]. Then one of them may be presumed, like the solitary report of a just narrator, for it is presumed [true] with the possibility of forgetfulness and oversight, and the solitary report of a habitual liar, for its falsehood is presumed with the possibility of truth, for a liar may sometimes tell the truth. And they may be equal in truth and falsehood, like the unknown [narrator], i.e., the solitary report of one whose justice and lying are unknown. This is what they said. But one may object that his report is proof according to some, indeed his testimony is accepted by the great Imam (may Allah be pleased with him), and his narration is also accepted according to what is reported from him in non-zahir al-riwayah, so how can his report be equal in truth and falsehood? Rather, it is presumed true, but the presumption is weak. Some of the Zahiriyya said: everything whose truth is not known, its falsehood is known. The apparent meaning is that they intended by it the certain matching [of reality], like the report of a claimant to prophethood. That is, they analogized to the report of a claimant to prophethood, for when his truth is not known through showing miracles, one is certain of his falsehood, because reports are equal. And this, i.e., the statement of the Zahiriyya, is false because it entails the negation of both contradictories, which necessitates their conjunction, because the falsehood of each necessitates the truth of the other, so the falsehood of both necessitates their truth. And there is no impossibility in the relationship between the impossible and its negation, rather it is the truth according to the well-known reductio ad absurdum arguments.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a classification of reports (akhbar) based on how we know their truth or falsehood. The author presents a Hanafi usul taxonomy: first, reports known true by necessity in themselves (mutawatir); second, reports known true by necessity through something else (like mathematical truths); third, reports known true by reasoning (like reports from Allah and the Messenger). For those who have reached spiritual realization, such reports are known by necessity. The report of the people of consensus (ahl al-ijma') in certainties also falls under reasoned knowledge. The classification then covers reports that are not known true with certainty: solitary reports with circumstantial evidence may yield knowledge if they are accompanied by enough indications. For reports that do not yield certainty, they fall into conjecture: the report of a just narrator is probable (maznun al-sidq), that of a habitual liar is probable falsehood, and that of an unknown narrator was said to be equal in probability, but the author objects that in the Hanafi school, such a report is still considered proof and thus is more likely true, albeit with weak probability. The author then refutes the Zahiriyya position that every report not known true is known false, using a reductio argument: if two unknown narrators report contradictory statements, and neither is known true, then according to the Zahiriyya both would be known false, leading to both contradictories being false, which is impossible. Therefore the Zahiriyya position is invalid. The Hanafi position is that reports are classified by levels of certainty, with a middle ground of probability.

Key Terms
ظاهرية (Zahiriyya): A school known for strict literal interpretation; here, a minority view that reports not known true are known false.
قياس خلفي (qiyas khalfi): A reductio ad absurdum argument: showing that a claim leads to an impossible conclusion, thus the claim is false.
نقيضان (naqidan): Two contradictory propositions that cannot both be true or both false.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core logical flaw in the Zahiriyya position according to the Hanafi response?
A) It assumes all reports are equal.
B) It leads to two contradictories being simultaneously false.
C) It ignores the possibility of circumstantial evidence.
D) It contradicts the definition of khabar.

Key Takeaway
The Zahiriyya claim that 'not known true implies known false' is falsified by a reductio argument, reinforcing the Hanafi principle of graded epistemic certainty.

Tawatur Yields Certain Knowledge: Hanafi Refutation of the Samaniyya
Proving tawatur yields certain knowledge, refuting five Samaniyya arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that mutawatir reports yield qat'i knowledge and refute the five arguments of the Samaniyya by applying the Hanafi responses.

Core Idea
Mutawatir reports yield certain knowledge because collusion on a lie is impossible, despite skeptics' sophistries.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut establishes that knowledge from tawatur is certain and necessary, directly opposing the Samaniyya sect from India who deny prophethood. The author presents a summary answer that their doubts are like sophistry against necessary knowledge, then provides detailed responses to their first three arguments. This lesson will walk you through the Hanafi proof and the refutation, highlighting the key analytical moves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
Locate the opening statement: 'Knowledge from tawatur is true and established.' This is the Hanafi position that tawatur yields certain knowledge (qat'i).
The claim is in direct opposition to the Samaniyya.
2
Examine the summary refutation
The author dismisses all five arguments as 'skepticism about the necessary' (تشكيك في الضروري). Understand that for the Hanafi, tawatur is a necessary source of knowledge, so any doubt is akin to sophistry.
This is a high-level rebuttal.
3
Analyze the first argument and response
The Samaniyya analogize tawatur to a group gathering for one meal, which is rare. The author responds with 'قياس مع الفارق' — there is a motive to report truth in tawatur (the habit of reporting what is known), unlike the appetite for food.
The key is the existence of a motive (dai) in the case of reports.
4
Analyze the second argument and response
The Samaniyya argue that if each individual could lie, so could the group. The author distinguishes between the ruling of the whole and the ruling of individuals; the collective context makes collusion on a single lie impossible.
He illustrates with the example of two opposites being possible individually but impossible together.
5
Analyze the third argument and response
The Samaniyya claim that if tawatur yields knowledge, two contradictory mutawatir reports would cause a paradox. The author replies that tawatur of opposites is impossible by custom (عادۃ), so no real contradiction occurs.
The discussion includes a subtle point about possibility of the collective versus individual.

قولهم (مكابرة) صريحة على العقل (ضرورة العلم بالبلاد النائية) كمكة والمدينة شرفهما الله تعالى (والأمم الخالية) كالأنبياء السابقين، وكأوس وكي قالوا: أولاً: إنه أي الأخبار تواتراً (كاجتماع الجمع على طعام واحد، وهو ممتنع عادة) فيستحيل الأخبار تواتراً، فلا يفيد العلم، إذ هو فرع التحقق، وهذه الشبهة تدل على أنهم أنكروا وجود التواتر أيضاً (و) قالوا: (ثانياً: يجوز الكذب على كل من المخبرين بتعمد أو نسيان أو (بنقيضين) كما إذا أخبر جمع بوجود اسكندر وآخر بعدمه، فلو كانا معلومين لكان موجوداً ومعدوماً في الواقع (و) قالوا (رابعاً) لو أفاد المتواتر علماً (يلزم تصديق اليهود أو النصارى فيما نقلوه) افتراء (عن موسى عليهما وعلى نبينا وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام) أنه قال: لا نبي بعدي والثاني باطل قطعاً، فإن هذا النقل كذب وافتراء بلا مرية (و) قالوا (خامساً) لو أفاد المتواتر العلم لما كان بينه وبين العلوم الأخر تفاوت ونجد التفاوت بينه وبين قولنا الواحد نصف الاثنين، وهو دليل احتمال النقيضين في المتواتر، فلا يفيد العلم و(الجواب عن شبهاتهم كلها (إجمالاً أنه تشكيك في الضروري) فإن كل أحد يعلم إفادة المتواتر العلم كشبه السوفسطائية) فإنها تشكيكات في الأمور الضرورية، فالشبهات جلها باطلة لا يلتفت إليها فافهم و(أما) الجواب عن شبهاتهم تفصيلاً فعن الدليل (الأول) وهو قياسهم على امتناع اجتماع الكل على أكل طعام أنه (قياس مع الفارق بين الفرع والأصل (الوجود الداعي) في أخبار الكل (وهو العادة ههنا) فإن عادة الإنسان أن يخبر بما يعلم (وعدمه) أي عدم الداعي (ثمة) أي في المقيس عليه، فإن الداعي إلى الأكل الاشتهاء، وقلما يكون اشتهاء الجماعة طعاماً واحداً عادة (وعن) الدليل (الثاني) وهو جواز الكذب قد يخالف حكم (الكل) أي المجموع) (حكم كل) أي كل واحد واحد (فللاجتماع أثر في الحكم فلا يوجد عند عدمه، وإذا كان حكماهما وهو رفعهما، أنه بالذات، قلت: رفع الكل أعم من رفعهما معاً، بل هو قد يكون برفع واحد لا بعينه ولا يلزم من وجوب الأعم وجوب الأخص، نعم يلزم وجوب أحدهما لامتناع الارتفاع وإن كان كل ممكناً، ولا يلزم من أفراد شيء إمكان مطلقه فافهم وعن الدليل الثالث وهو لزوم اجتماع النقيضين عند إمكان جميع أخبار الجماعة بخبرين متناقضين إن تواتر النقيضين محال عادة فلا يلزم التناقض في الواقع، بل على تقدير خلاف الواقع فلا استحالة. فإن قلت: الأخبار بالمتناقضين وإن كان خلاف العادة لكنه ممكن بالذات لا يلزم من فرضه محال، ولو فرض ههنا لزم المحال وهو التناقض، فحصول العلم بالتواتر محال لأنه ما لزم المحال إلا منه قلت لا نسلم إمكانه بالذات، بل
Issue: Knowledge of tawatur is true and established (contrary to the Samaniyya of the Brahmins). It is well-known that they are a different sect from the Brahmins; they are worshippers of Somnath (name of an idol broken by Sultan Mahmud bin Sabuktegin). The Samaniyya are a people from India who deny prophethood. Their statement is open obstinacy against reason, because of the necessity of knowing distant lands like Mecca and Medina (may Allah honor them) and past nations like earlier prophets, and like Aws and Kay. They said: First, that tawatur is like a group gathering over a single meal, which is habitually impossible, thus tawatur is impossible, so it does not yield knowledge. This suspicion indicates they also deny the existence of tawatur. Second, that lying is possible for each informer intentionally or by forgetfulness or negligence, so likewise lies are possible for all collectively by consensus, because the whole is just the individuals collectively, so its ruling is their ruling. If lying is possible, there is no knowledge. Third, if tawatur yielded knowledge, it would lead to contradiction if two large groups report two contradictory things, as if a group reports the existence of Alexander and another his non-existence. If both were known, he would be existent and non-existent in reality. Fourth, if tawatur yielded knowledge, it would necessitate believing the Jews or Christians in what they falsely transmitted about Moses (peace be upon him and our Prophet) that he said: 'No prophet after me' and the second is definitively false, so this transmission is a lie without doubt. Fifth, if tawatur yielded knowledge, there would be no difference between it and other sciences, but we find a difference between it and our statement 'one is half of two', which indicates the possibility of contradictory conclusions, so tawatur does not yield knowledge. The answer to all their suspicions in summary is that it is skepticism about the necessary. For everyone knows that tawatur yields knowledge, like the sophist doubts. Most of the suspicions are false and are to be ignored. As for the detailed answer: First, their analogy to the impossibility of a group gathering over one meal is an analogy with a difference between the branch and the root: There is an existence of a motive in the case of reports (the habit here is that a person informs of what he knows) and the absence of motive there (the motive for eating is appetite, and rarely does a whole group desire one meal habitually). Second, regarding the possibility of lying, the ruling of the whole may differ from the ruling of each individual. For the gathering has an effect in the ruling, so it cannot be found when it is absent. Since their rulings differ, the possibility of lying for each does not necessitate the possibility of lying for all. Then he gave an example: Do you not see that each of the two opposites is possible (for existence) unlike the whole, for it is impossible and not possible. If you say: If each of the two opposites were not possible, then their negation would be necessary, which is raising both? No, rather raising the whole is more general than raising both together, indeed it may be by raising one not specified. The necessity of the general does not necessitate the necessity of the specific. Third, regarding the impossibility of contradictory reports: Tawatur of two contradictory reports is habitually impossible, so contradiction does not occur in reality. Even if contrary to reality, no impossibility. If you say: Reporting contradictories even if contrary to habit is possible in itself, and if supposed here it leads to the impossible (contradiction), so obtaining knowledge from tawatur is impossible because the impossible only results from it. I say: We do not accept its possibility in itself, but...
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage addresses the epistemological status of mutawatir reports. The author (the commentator) asserts that tawatur yields certain knowledge, opposing the Samaniyya, a group of Indian atheists who deny prophethood and argue that tawatur is not reliable. The Samaniyya present five arguments: (1) impossibility of a large group unanimously reporting the same thing (analogy to rare agreement on food), (2) possibility of lying individually extends to the group, (3) tawatur would lead to contradiction if two groups report opposites, (4) belief in false transmissions from Jews/Christians, (5) difference between tawatur-based knowledge and certain logical truths. The author gives a summary answer that these are sophistical doubts against necessary knowledge. Then detailed answers: (1) the analogy is flawed because there is a motive to report truth but not necessarily to eat same food; (2) the whole's ruling differs from individuals because the group context precludes collusion on a lie; (3) tawatur of opposites is impossible by habit; (4) not covered in detail in this passage; (5) the text cuts off. The passage exemplifies the Hanafi usul position that tawatur is a definitive source of knowledge.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report narrated by such a large number that it is impossible for them to collude on a lie, yielding certain knowledge.
السمنية (al-samaniyya): A group from India who deny prophethood and question the reliability of tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because eating is a different category from news.
B) Because there is no motive for a group to report truth.
C) Because there is a motive to report truth, unlike the motive for eating.
D) Because the Samaniyya are lying.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that mutawatir reports yield certain knowledge, and the skeptics' arguments are invalid due to false analogies and disregard for necessary knowledge.

The Relationship Between Conditions of Tawatur: Refuting Ibn al-Hajib's Claim
Analyzing logical relationship between conditions of tawatur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the condition of a sufficient number in one generation does not entail the other conditions of tawatur, and articulate the Hanafi position on the interdependence of conditions.

Core Idea
The number condition alone does not guarantee tawatur; each condition is independently necessary.

In this passage, the commentator responds to a claim by Ibn al-Hajib that if the number of reporters is sufficient to prevent collusion, then the other two conditions (presence in every generation and reliance on sense) are automatically fulfilled. This lesson unpacks the refutation and clarifies the Hanafi understanding that each condition is separate and must be independently satisfied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Ibn al-Hajib argued that stipulating the first condition (sufficient number in one generation) makes the last two conditions (same number in all generations and sense perception) redundant. Understand the logical structure: the first condition is supposed to entail the last two.
The claim is based on the idea that if the number prevents collusion, it must be in sensed matters and in all generations.
2
Analyze the refutation
The commentator explains that the first condition only refers to the existence of the number in a single generation. It does not guarantee that the same number exists in all generations, nor does it guarantee the report is about sensed matters. The prevention of collusion only occurs after all conditions are met.
The key is that the first condition is not a sufficient condition for the others; it is merely a necessary condition.
3
Understand the consequence
If the first condition were sufficient, then tawatur could be established by a single generation of reporters, which contradicts the Hanafi requirement of continuity. The logical relationship between conditions is clarified: each is independently necessary.
The commentator uses the phrase 'هكذا ينبغي أن يفهم' to emphasize correct understanding.
4
Summarize the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that tawatur requires three independent conditions: (1) sufficient number in at least one generation to prevent collusion, (2) that number in every generation, and (3) the report must be about sensed matters. None of these conditions can substitute for another.
This analysis is foundational for understanding why the minimum number is not fixed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بعد تحقق شرائط أخرى، حتى لا يحتاج منع التواطؤ إلى عدد أزيد منه وليس المراد امتناع التواطؤ في الحال حتى يرد عليه أن ذلك متضمن لسائر الشرائط، فهو ملزوم لها (وحينئذ ظهر أن الأول ليس بملزوم للأخيرين هكذا ينبغي أن يفهم) هذا المقام (ثم اختلف في أقل العدد المشروط في التواتر (فقيل : أربعة قياساً على شهود الزنا) فإنه أمر عظيم وقد أمرنا بالدرء بالشبهات ولا شك أن غير المتواتر مما فيه شبهة، فعلم أن الأربعة مفيدة للقطع (وقيل) ذلك العدد (خمسة قياساً على اللعان) فإنه خمس شهادات، وإذا قبل إخبار رجل خمس مرات وأفاد اليقين فإخبار خمسة رجال بالطريق الأولى (وقطع القاضي) الباقلاني بنفي الأربعة، إذ لو (أفاد خبر الأربعة اليقين لم تحتج شهود الزنا إلى التزكية) لأن العدالة غير معتبرة في التواتر وفيه تأمل ويرد عليه وروداً ظاهراً أن التزكية في الشهادة أمر تعبدي لا لتحصيل اليقين، ألا ترى أن سبعين ألفاً لو شهدوا مثل هذا العدد يفيد العلم) (بغير تلك الواقعة لشخص آخر) فلو كان الأربعة مفيداً للعلم في الواقعة لأفاد في الزنا، فلا يحتاج إلى التزكية (وفيه وما فيه) فإنه باطل بالضرورة، كيف والإفادة تختلف باختلاف المخبر عنه والمخبرين وغير ذلك، وربما يؤوّل بأن كل عدد أفاد علماً بواقعة فمثل هذا العدد في الأحوال العارضة لها، وعلى هذا لا يكفي في دفع الإيراد، فإنه لما كان مشاهدة الزنا بعيداً في العادة لكونه في الأكثر في مكان خال لم تفد الأربعة ويجوز أن تفيد في غيره مما تسهل فيه المشاهدة فتدبر ( وتردد) القاضي (في الخمسة) ولم يقطع بانتفائه (ويرد عليه أن وجوب التزكية مشترك بين الأربعة والخمسة إذا شهدوا بالزنا، فيجب أن لا تفيد العلم أيضاً، بل يجب أن لا يتحقق تواتر أصلاً، فإن كل عدد لو شهدوا بالزنا وجب تزكيتهم (إلا) أن يقول القاضي حال كونه فارقاً) بين الصورتين كل خمسة صادقة) قد تفيد العلم) بما أخبروا (فإذا لم تفد) العلم (في الزنا علم أن فيهم كذوباً أي من شأنه أن يكذب، لكنه غير معلوم بالتعين لا أن فيهم كذوباً في الأخبار حتى يقال : كذب واحد يستلزم كذب الكل، لأن كلامهم واحد فالتزكية تعلم صدق الباقي وهو النصاب فلم يلزم منه أن أخبار الخمسة الصادقة غير مفيد بل بقي الاحتمال كما كان بخلاف (الأربعة فإن التزكية فيهم ليس لهذا فإنه إذا علم كذوبية واحد لم يبق الباقي نصاباً فلا تفيد التزكية والتزكية واجبة قطعاً، فليس إلا لأنّ الأربعة غير مفيدة للعلم قطعاً، فاتضح الفرق فتدبر) فإنه غاية ما يوجه به كلام القاضي، لكن بقي فيه شيء، فإنه قد مر أن كل عدد يفيد العلم في واقعة مفيد في جميع الوقائع، فلو الخمسة في واقعة لأفاد في الزنا أيضاً وحينئذ لا تصح التزكية فإذا لم تفد لم يعلم أن فيهم كذوباً بل علم أنه لا يفيد في واقعة أصلاً، وكونه من شأنه أن يكذب لا ينافي حصول العلم، فإن العدالة غير معتبرة في التواتر فافهم (وقيل) أقل العدد المعتبر (سبعة قياساً على غسل الإناء من ولوغ الكلب سبع مرات قال النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «إذا شرب الكلب في إناء أحدكم فليغسله سبعاً رواه البخاري، وهذا الحديث منسوخ عندنا بحديث الاكتفاء بالثلاث في غسل النجاسات، كما بين في موضعه وجه القياس أن للسبعة تأثيراً في التطهير، واليقين أيضاً تطهير فتأمل فإن فيه ما فيه (وقيل) أقل العدد المشروط في التواتر (عشرة لقوله تعالى : ﴿ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ [البقرة : ١٩٦] حيث وصف العشرة بالكمال فيكون مفيداً للعلم (وقيل) أقله اثنا عشر عدد نقباء بني إسرائيل حيث جعلهم موسى على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام أمناء وأرسلهم ليعرفوا من أخبار الجبابرة ولولا أن خبرهم مفيد للعلم لما بعثهم لذلك (وقيل) أقله (عشرون ، قال تعالى: ﴿إِن يَكُن مِّنكُمْ عِشْرُونَ صَبِرُونَ يَغْلِبُوا مِائَتَيْنِ [الأنفال : ٦٥]) حيث فرض عليهم الجهاد لما كان خبرهم بمجيء الرسول، وإيجابه الأيمان مفيداً للعلم، حتى وجب قتالهم بالمخالفة عنهم (وقيل) أقله (أربعون ) قال عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام: (خير السرايا أربعون وليست الخيرية إلا لأن خبرهم مفيد للعلم حتى وجب القتال بمخالفتهم (وقيل) أقله (خمسون قياساً على القسامة فإن فيها أخبار خمسين رجلاً إنهم ما قتلوا وما عرفوا قاتلاً، فتخصيص الخمسين إنما هو لكون خبرهم مفيداً للعلم دون الأقل منهم (وقيل) أقله سبعون لاختيار (موسى) على نبينا وعليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام سبعين رجلاً لميقاته حتى يسمعوا كلام الله تعالى ويخبروا من وراءهم، فلولا خبرهم مفيد للعلم لاختار أكثر ، ولو كان خبر الأقل مفيداً لاكتفى بهم (وقيل) أقله (أزيد من ثلثمائة
For if they report a report that they sensed it, their knowledge necessarily follows. I say: the intended meaning of reliance on sense is that the report is about sensed matters, not that they reported that they sensed it. So there is no sufficiency, so reflect. (It was said) in the marginalia of Mirzajan: if the condition of the necessary condition were sufficient for the condition of the necessary, as Ibn al-Hajib said, then the condition of the first (that the reporters reach a number that prevents collusion on falsehood) would make the last two (that they are such in every generation and reliance on sense) unnecessary. Because if the number of reporters reaches a limit that prevents the mind from agreeing on falsehood, that only happens in sensed matters, for in intellectual matters it is not impossible to agree on falsehood. And the middle and ends must be equal, otherwise agreement would be possible. But the sufficiency of the condition of the necessary for the necessary is established, so the negation of the condition of the last two follows. Or it is said: the sufficiency of the first for the last two is false, so the sufficiency of the necessary for the necessary is false. Then the last is needed even if the first entails it. On the first interpretation, it is an objection to the majority like Ibn al-Hajib's objection; on the second, it is a response to Ibn al-Hajib's objection. I say: this statement is not valid regardless, rather the intended meaning of the first condition is the existence of the number in the mentioned limit in some generation. As for its existence in all generations, that is from the third condition, and there is no doubt that the first does not entail this. And the intended meaning of 'preventing the mind' from collusion on falsehood is its prevention after the existence of the other conditions. That is, the intended meaning is the gathering of the number in terms of multitude, even if this prevention occurs after other conditions are realized, so that preventing collusion does not need a larger number than it. And the intended meaning is not the prevention of collusion at the moment, such that it would be objected that this includes the other conditions, so it is entailing them. Then it becomes clear that the first is not entailing the last two. This is how this point should be understood. Then they differed on the minimum number stipulated in tawatur. It was said: four, by analogy to witnesses of adultery, for it is a great matter and we are commanded to avoid doubts, and there is no doubt that non-mutawatir involves doubt, so it is known that four produce certainty. And it was said: that number is five, by analogy to li'an, for it is five testimonies, and if the report of one man five times is accepted and produces certainty, then the report of five men is even more apt. And al-Qadi al-Baqillani decisively negated four, because if the report of four produced certainty, the witnesses of adultery would not need tazkiyah (validation of character), since justice is not considered in tawatur. In this there is consideration. And it is objected to him manifestly that tazkiyah in testimony is a devotional matter, not for obtaining certainty. Do you not see that if seventy thousand testified to adultery, tazkiyah would still be obligatory. Hence, if certainty is obtained not from witnesses, the hadd penalty is not obligatory. Hence, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) did not stone that woman and said: 'If I were to stone without witnesses, I would have stoned this one.' Reported by al-Bukhari. If you say: the utmost of his proof is that four do not produce certainty in adultery, and it does not imply that they do not produce certainty in another case, he said: 'That is, the proof of al-Qadi is based on what he said, and Abu al-Husayn from the Mu'tazila agreed with him, that every number that gives knowledge of an incident to a person, then the same number gives knowledge of a different incident to another person.' So if four gave knowledge of an incident, they would give knowledge in adultery, so tazkiyah would not be needed. In this there is much to say, for it is invalid necessarily. How so? Because giving knowledge differs according to the reported matter, the reporters, and other factors. Perhaps it is interpreted that every number that gives knowledge of an incident gives knowledge of the same type of incident in incidental matters. Even so, this does not suffice to repel the objection, because since witnessing adultery is usually rare, often in a secluded place, four do not give knowledge, but they might give knowledge in other matters where witnessing is easier. So ponder. And al-Qadi was hesitant about five and did not decisively negate it. And it is objected to him that the obligation of tazkiyah is common between four and five if they testify to adultery, so they should also not give knowledge. Rather, tawatur should not occur at all, because every number, if they testify to adultery, must be validated, unless al-Qadi says, distinguishing between the two cases: 'Every truthful five might give knowledge of what they reported. So if they do not give knowledge in adultery, it is known that among them is a liar, i.e., someone who is prone to lie, but not specifically known, not that among them is a liar in the reports such that it would be said: one lie entails the lie of all, because their speech is one. So tazkiyah informs of the truthfulness of the rest, who constitute the required number. So it does not follow from this that the report of truthful five is not beneficial; rather, the probability remains as it was. Unlike four, for tazkiyah with them is not for this reason, because if the lying of one is known, the rest do not constitute the required number, so tazkiyah is not beneficial. And tazkiyah is absolutely obligatory, so it is only because four do not produce knowledge absolutely. So the difference is clear, ponder.' This is the utmost by which the words of al-Qadi are directed. But there remains something: it has been mentioned that every number that gives knowledge in one incident gives knowledge in all incidents. So if five give knowledge in one incident, they would give knowledge in adultery also. Then tazkiyah would not be valid. So if they do not give knowledge, it is not known that there is a liar among them; rather, it is known that they do not give knowledge in any incident at all. And being prone to lie does not prevent the attainment of knowledge, for justice is not considered in tawatur. So understand. And it was said: the minimum number considered is seven, by analogy to washing a vessel from a dog's licking seven times. The Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'If a dog drinks from the vessel of one of you, let him wash it seven times.' Reported by al-Bukhari. This hadith is abrogated in our view by the hadith of sufficing with three in washing impurities, as explained in its place. The point of analogy is that seven has an effect in purification, and certainty is also purification. So reflect, for there is much in it. And it was said: the minimum number stipulated in tawatur is ten, due to the Almighty's saying: 'Those are ten complete' (Quran 2:196) where He described ten as complete, so it gives knowledge. And it was said: its minimum is twelve, the number of the chiefs of the Children of Israel, for Moses (peace be upon our Prophet and upon him) made them trustees and sent them to learn news of the tyrants. Had their report not given knowledge, he would not have sent them for that. And it was said: its minimum is twenty. The Almighty said: 'If there are among you twenty steadfast, they will overcome two hundred' (Quran 8:65) where He enjoined jihad upon them because their report of the arrival of the messenger and the imposition of oaths gave knowledge, such that fighting them was obligatory when they opposed. And it was said: its minimum is forty. He (peace be upon him and upon his family and companions) said: 'The best of expeditions is forty.' The best is only because their report gives knowledge, such that fighting was obligatory when they opposed. And it was said: its minimum is fifty, by analogy to the qasamah (oath of fifty), for in it fifty men swear that they did not kill and do not know the killer. The specification of fifty is because their report gives knowledge, unlike fewer. And it was said: its minimum is seventy, because Moses (peace be upon our Prophet and upon him and upon his family and companions) chose seventy men for his appointment to hear the speech of Allah and inform those behind them. Had their report not given knowledge, he would have chosen more. And if the report of fewer gave knowledge, he would have sufficed with them. And it was said: its minimum is more than three hundred.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for tawatur (mutawatir transmission) and the disputed minimum number of transmitters required to produce certain knowledge. The commentator, Abd al-Ali al-Ansari, begins by analyzing a claim made by Ibn al-Hajib and the marginalia of Mirzajan that the condition of the number in one generation (the first condition) is sufficient to dispense with the conditions that this number be present in every generation (the second condition) and that the report be based on sense perception (the third condition). The commentator refutes this, explaining that the first condition refers only to the number in a single generation, not that it guarantees the other conditions. He then clarifies that the prevention of collusion on falsehood only occurs after all other conditions are met. The passage then transitions to the disagreement over the minimum number for tawatur. The text lists and evaluates various opinions: four (by analogy to witnesses of adultery), five (by analogy to li'an), seven (by analogy to washing a vessel from a dog's licking, though this hadith is considered abrogated in the Hanafi school), ten (quoting Q. 2:196 'those are ten complete'), twelve (the number of Israelite chiefs), twenty (from Q. 8:65), forty (from a hadith about the best expedition), fifty (by analogy to qasamah), seventy (from the story of Moses), and more than three hundred (from a hadith about the number of Companions at the pledge of Ridwan). The commentator provides critical analysis of al-Qadi al-Baqillani's position on four and five, showing the weaknesses in his reasoning. The passage does not explicitly adopt any one number, but the critical remarks suggest that the number is not fixed; rather, the condition is that the number must be such that collusion on falsehood is impossible, which may vary.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur): A report transmitted by such a large number of narrators in each generation that it is impossible for them to have colluded on a falsehood, thus producing certain knowledge.
شرط التواتر (sharṭ al-tawātur): The conditions that must be satisfied for a report to be mutawatir: sufficient number in at least one generation, continuity of that number, and sense basis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is Ibn al-Hajib's claim that the first condition suffices for the last two invalid?
A) Because the first condition does not guarantee the report is about sensed matters.
B) Because the first condition only applies to a single generation, not to all generations.
C) Because the last two conditions are not necessary for tawatur.
D) Because the first condition is not a condition at all.

Key Takeaway
The three conditions of tawatur are independently necessary; a sufficient number in one generation does not automatically ensure continuity or sense basis.

8 min
The Disputed Minimum Number for Tawatur: From Four to Over Three Hundred
Surveying and critically evaluating opinions on the minimum number for tawatur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the various opinions on the minimum number of transmitters for tawatur, evaluate the evidence for each, and explain the Hanafi position that no fixed number is required.

Core Idea
There is no fixed number for tawatur; the condition is the impossibility of collusion, which varies by context.

After establishing the conditions of tawatur, the passage turns to the heated debate over the specific minimum number. Opinions range from four to over three hundred, each supported by analogies or textual references. The commentator critically examines these arguments, ultimately pointing to the Hanafi view that the number is not fixed but depends on the context and the impossibility of collusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major opinions
List the numbers mentioned: 4, 5, 7, 10, 12, 20, 40, 50, 70, and >300. For each, note the evidence cited (Quran, hadith, qiyas).
The passage does not claim any of these numbers as definitive; they are presented as opinions of various scholars and schools.
2
Analyze the evidence for each number
For each opinion, understand the basis: e.g., 4 from witnesses of adultery (qiyas), 5 from li'an (qiyas), 10 from Quran 2:196 (dalalat al-nass), etc. Consider the commentator's critical remarks.
Some analogies are weak, and some hadith are abrogated (like the 7 washes).
3
Examine the critique of al-Qadi al-Baqillani’s position on four and five
Al-Baqillani argued that if 4 produced certainty, witnesses of adultery would not need tazkiyah. The commentator refutes this by noting tazkiyah is devotional, not epistemic. For 5, the commentator shows that the objection applies similarly, but al-Baqillani was hesitant.
The critique highlights that epistemic certainty and legal requirements are distinct.
4
Formulate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school does not adopt any fixed number. The key is that the number must be sufficient to prevent collusion on falsehood, which may vary depending on the report, the reporters, and the circumstances.
This is consistent with the earlier analysis that the conditions are independent and contextual.

فإنهم إذا أخبروا بخبر بأنهم أحسوا به لزم علمهم قطعاً قلت المراد بالاستناد إلى الحس أن يكون الخبر في المحسوسات لا أنهم أخبروا بأنهم أحسوا فلا إغناء فتأمل، (قيل) في حواشي ميرزاجان لو كان اشتراط الملزوم مغنياً عن اشتراط اللازم) كما قال ابن الحاجب (أغنى اشتراط (الأول وهو بلوغ المخبرين عدداً يمتنع تواطؤهم على الكذب (عن الأخيرين) كونهم كذلك في كل طبقة، والاستناد إلى الحس لأنه إذا بلغ عدد المخبرين حداً يمنع العقل الاتفاق على الكذب لا يكون ذلك إلا في المحسوس فإن العقلي لا يمتنع فيه الاتفاق على الكذب ويلزم استواء الوسط والطرفين وإلا جاز الاتفاق، لكن إغناء اشتراط الملزوم عن اللازم ثابت فيلزم انتفاء اشتراط الأخيرين أو يقال : إن إغناء اشتراط الأول الأخيرين عن باطل، فيلزم بطلان إغناء اشتراط الملزوم عن اشتراط اللازم وحينئذ فيحتاج إلى الأخير وإن كان الأول مستلزماً إياه فعلى الأول إيراد على الجمهور مثل إيراد ابن الحاجب وعلى الثاني : جواب عن إيراد ابن الحاجب (أقول ) لا يصح هذا الكلام كيفما كان، بل (المراد من الشرط الأول وجود المبلغ في الحد المذكور (في طبقة ما من الطبقات (وأما) وجود هذا المبلغ (في جميع الطبقات فمن الشرط الثالث ولا شك في عدم لزوم هذا من الأول (والمراد بمنع العقل) التواطأ على الكذب ومنعه بعد وجود سائر الشرائط) يعني أن المراد منه اجتماع العدد من جهة الكثرة، ولو كان يحصل هذا المنع بعد تحقق شرائط أخرى، حتى لا يحتاج منع التواطؤ إلى عدد أزيد منه وليس المراد امتناع التواطؤ في الحال حتى يرد عليه أن ذلك متضمن لسائر الشرائط، فهو ملزوم لها (وحينئذ ظهر أن الأول ليس بملزوم للأخيرين هكذا
